- **ADR-075 mobile delivery — offline behaviour + single-slot pending send (founder ask 2026-04-25 «при отсутствии сети не падать на 404, а показывать стилизованную страницу; при нестабильной сети ставить сообщение со значком загрузка → повторить/отмена как в Telegram»; code-landed; verification gate green; awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live mobile gates):** ADR-075 was extended with two new top-level sections — `## Offline behaviour` and `## Single-slot pending send` — and the corresponding implementation landed across both repos. **Offline behaviour (two layers).** `persai-mobile/capacitor.config.ts` now sets `server.errorPath: "offline.html"` so a cold-start network failure hands the WebView to a self-contained `persai-mobile/www/offline.html` (inline CSS + JS, no React, no bundled fonts; respects `prefers-color-scheme: dark`; localises into `en` / `ru` from `navigator.language`; "Try again" calls `window.location.reload()` so a successful retry seamlessly re-enters `apps/web` via `server.url`). Mid-session drops are caught by a new web-side hook `apps/web/app/app/_components/use-network-online.ts` (combines `navigator.onLine` with `online`/`offline` events, plus a `recheck()` action that performs a no-cache `fetch("/api/health")` so the user can force re-evaluation without waiting for the OS to fire `online`) consumed by `apps/web/app/app/_components/offline-gate.tsx`, mounted once near the root in `apps/web/app/app/_components/app-shell.tsx`. The overlay shares the same copy as the cold-start page (i18n keys under `offline` in `apps/web/messages/{en,ru}.json` — `title` / `message` / `retry` / `rechecking`) and keeps app state mounted underneath so closing it resumes whatever the user was doing. **Single-slot pending send.** `ChatMessageStatus` (in `apps/web/app/app/_components/use-chat.ts`) gains two states `sending` and `send_failed`; `useChat` exposes `pendingSendStatus`, `retryPendingSend()`, and `cancelPendingSend()` as the wiring surface. **Pre-flight gates** — when `navigator.onLine === false` at submit time the user bubble is added with `status: "send_failed"` immediately and no fetch is attempted; while a previous send is in `send_failed` `useChat.send()` is a no-op and `chat-input.tsx` reflects this with a disabled Send button, a destructive-toned helper line ("Message hasn't been delivered. Retry or cancel to send a new one."), and Enter-to-send gating. **In-flight watchdogs** — attachment uploads (`stageWebChatAttachment`, `transcribeVoice`) now go through the new XHR helper `apps/web/app/app/upload-with-progress.ts` which exposes a 15s **stall watchdog** (`XhrStallError` when no progress for 15s — smart for big uploads on weak signal because bytes-keep-moving keeps it alive) and a 5min **hard upper bound** (`XhrTimeoutError`); the stream turn (`streamAssistantWebChatTurn`) gets a 10s **pre-headers timeout** in `useChat.send()` with `onHeadersOk` as the success signal (`response.ok` ⇒ server accepted the request; we do not impose a wall-clock cap on the post-headers stream because tool turns can legitimately run 30–60s). **UI surface (Telegram-style, intentionally quiet)** — `chat-message.tsx` user bubble in `sending` shows a 12px `Loader2` + "Sending…"; in `send_failed` it shows an `AlertCircle` + "Not delivered" plus two compact text-buttons **Retry** (re-runs the same payload — same text, same `File[]`, same `addToKnowledgeBase` flag — through `retryPendingSend()`) and **Cancel** (`cancelPendingSend()` removes the bubble and, for text messages, restores the draft text into the composer via a new imperative `ChatInputHandle.setDraft` ref so the user does not lose what they typed). `chat-input.tsx` was converted to `forwardRef<ChatInputHandle, _>` to expose `setDraft`. **Persistence:** failed-bubble state is in-memory and per-thread (switching chats discards the failed bubble; reloading the app does the same — deliberate simplification because persisting failed sends across cold starts would force us to also persist the `File`/`Blob` payloads, doubling storage costs). **Tests.** New `pending-send slot (ADR-075)` describe block in `apps/web/app/app/_components/use-chat.test.tsx` covers six scenarios: offline pre-flight flips bubble to `send_failed` without calling `streamAssistantWebChatTurn`; second send is blocked while previous is `send_failed`; `onHeadersOk` flips bubble to `committed` and clears the pending slot; pre-headers abort flips bubble to `send_failed` and removes the assistant placeholder; `retryPendingSend` re-dispatches the same payload and clears the slot on success; `cancelPendingSend` returns the draft text and removes the bubble. Existing `chat-area.test.tsx` mock chat extended with the three new return fields. Total `apps/web` suite is now 100/100 passing (was 94/94). **Verification gate green** — `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean, `pnpm run format:check` clean (5 files re-formatted by prettier on first pass), `pnpm --filter @persai/web run typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/api run typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/web run test` 100/100. **Awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live mobile gates** (drop airplane mode while typing → bubble flips to send_failed without hanging; Retry recovers same payload; Cancel restores draft; cold-launch with no network shows the stylised `offline.html` instead of the platform error chrome).

- **ADR-075 mobile delivery via Capacitor WebView shell — accepted and live-verified on Android (founder verified spike + post-spike Back rework on Samsung SM-F966B Galaxy Z Fold 6 over USB ADB; production rollout still pending):** mobile delivery for PersAI now ships as a thin Capacitor 8 WebView shell loading the live `https://persai.dev` origin, hosted in a separate sibling repo `persai-mobile` rather than as a workspace package inside `PersAI`. The web origin stays the single source of UI truth — no static SPA bundle, no SSR re-implementation, Clerk proxy mode (`/clerk-proxy`) and same-origin BFF (`/api/v1`) keep working unchanged because everything stays on `persai.dev`. The Russian ISP blocking workaround inherits automatically. **Cross-platform UX additions in `apps/web` from this program** (commits `2ef74e97`, `2eb6929f`, `4528ec09`): two new hooks under `apps/web/app/app/_components/` — `useTouchDevice()` for `(hover: none) and (pointer: coarse)` feature detection (SSR-safe, hardened against jsdom's missing `matchMedia` for unit tests) and `useHistoryBackToClose(open, onClose)` for system-Back overlay close. Touch-friendly UX corrections that surfaced on the spike now benefit narrow-viewport desktop browser users too: composer Enter inserts a newline on touch and submits via the Send button (`chat-input.tsx`), assistant message body uses `min-w-0 max-w-full break-words [overflow-wrap:anywhere]` and the chat scroll container adds `overflow-x-hidden` (`chat-message.tsx`, `chat-area.tsx`) so long unbreakable strings no longer cause horizontal scroll, sidebar/chat-area kebab menus use `opacity-70` on touch viewports and `md:opacity-0 md:group-hover:opacity-100` on desktop. **Hardware Back is JS-driven via `@capacitor/app`** — the spike first tried a manual `MainActivity.onBackPressed()` override that delegated to `WebView.goBack()`, but it stopped firing on Android 14+ where the method is deprecated and the new `OnBackPressedDispatcher` interacts unpredictably with Next.js App Router pushState entries inside a WebView (effectively dead Back button). The shipped design replaced it with a pure-JS resolution chain: `apps/web/app/app/_components/back-button-bridge.tsx` mounts once near the App Router root and subscribes to `@capacitor/app`'s `backButton` event; `apps/web/app/app/_components/back-handler-stack.ts` is a module-level LIFO stack where modals/lightboxes/sidebars register a close handler on open and pop on close; resolution order is "topmost overlay handler → `window.history.back()` if `canGoBack` → `App.exitApp()` at the root". An earlier overlay-close implementation pushed marker history entries on open and listened for `popstate`; that approach worked for leaf modals but corrupted history whenever the overlay also contained a `router.push` link (mobile sidebar tapping a chat) — the back-handler-stack approach has no history side effects so it composes cleanly with router pushes inside an open overlay. **Native shell capabilities in `persai-mobile`.** Android `AndroidManifest.xml` declares `INTERNET` / `RECORD_AUDIO` / `MODIFY_AUDIO_SETTINGS` for `MediaRecorder`-based voice input, plus `WRITE_EXTERNAL_STORAGE` (`android:maxSdkVersion="28"`) for legacy `DownloadManager` on API ≤ 28, and a `FileProvider` (`${applicationId}.fileprovider`, `xml/file_paths.xml`) for sharing downloaded attachments. iOS `Info.plist` declares `NSMicrophoneUsageDescription`, `NSCameraUsageDescription`, `NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription`. `MainActivity#handleDownload` attaches an Android `DownloadListener` that re-issues every attachment URL through `DownloadManager` with the WebView's session cookie (so the proxy `/api/attachment/[id]` route can verify the user) and writes to `/Download` with a system notification; `Intent.ACTION_VIEW` last-resort fallback covers `data:` URIs. `capacitor.config.ts`: `appId="com.persai.app"`, `server.url="https://persai.dev"`, `cleartext: false`, `allowNavigation: ["persai.dev","*.persai.dev","accounts.google.com","*.googleusercontent.com"]` so OAuth round-trips stay inside the WebView, `android.allowMixedContent: false`, `ios.contentInset: "always"`. **Repo and ownership boundary.** `persai-mobile` owns Capacitor config, Android/iOS native projects, app icons/splash, native permission strings, store listings — no business logic. Mobile-specific UX branches inside `apps/web` via `useTouchDevice()` or feature detection, never in the shell. PersAI verification gates (`pnpm -r --if-present run lint`, `pnpm run format:check`, `pnpm --filter @persai/web run typecheck`, `pnpm --filter @persai/api run typecheck`) stay free of native toolchain dependencies. **Verified end-to-end on Z Fold 6** (founder, 2026-04-23 → live re-verified 2026-04-25): email sign-in through Clerk proxy on `persai.dev`, voice message via `MediaRecorder` (record / upload / transcribe / assistant reply), assistant streaming response in real time, session persists across cold-restart, JS-driven hardware Back closes overlays / navigates App Router history / exits at root same on Android 13/14/15, attachment download surfaces system Downloads notification and lands the file in `/Download`. **Pre-installed-for-next-slice dependencies in `apps/web`.** `@capacitor/camera ^8.1.0` and `@capacitor/network ^8.0.1` are now in `apps/web/package.json` and `pnpm-lock.yaml`. Neither is referenced from any source file yet — they are pre-installed under the same JS-glue model as `@capacitor/app` (the Back-button bridge): the JS plugin lives in the web codebase, the native side is registered automatically via `cap sync`. Camera will surface a richer in-app camera-capture path (the current `<input type="file" accept="image/*" capture>` works but is platform-default); network will let `apps/web` detect offline state and render a graceful placeholder instead of a blank WebView when `persai.dev` is unreachable. ADR-075's "Open questions" already flags both as deferred work; the install lands ahead of the wiring so the next slice can start without a Capacitor sync round-trip. **Production rollout still pending** — production web origin selection (likely `app.persai.com`), `allowNavigation` tightening, production icons/splash, Google Play Console internal track, Apple Developer account + first TestFlight, push notifications path decision (APNs/FCM via `@capacitor/push-notifications` vs keeping Telegram as the async channel) — all tracked in ADR-075's "Production rollout plan" + "Open questions" sections. ADR-075 was updated 2026-04-25 to reflect the post-spike JS-driven Back rework and DownloadManager attachment path; the Status block now reads "Accepted (spike verified end-to-end on Android; live-verified by founder; production rollout pending)".

- **Scheduled assistant checks now validate their terminal outcome instead of treating any completed hidden turn as success (founder live repro 2026-04-23: `assistant_check` fired, ran `web_search`, then completed empty so no push/user task was created):** the runtime already returns `toolInvocations` in `RuntimeTurnResult`, but `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/send-native-web-chat-turn.service.ts` was discarding them and `RunScheduledAssistantActionService` was equating "runtime call did not throw" with "background check completed correctly". That left a silent hole where a hidden run could do intermediate work (`web_search`) and then end with empty `assistantText`, no `scheduled_action`, and still be logged as `scheduled_assistant_action_completed`. Fix: `AssistantRuntimeWebChatTurnResult` now carries optional `toolInvocations`, `SendNativeWebChatTurnService` forwards them from runtime, and `RunScheduledAssistantActionService` validates the terminal state machine. A hidden `assistant_check` is now considered successful only if it either (a) created a successful `scheduled_action` follow-up or (b) returned a non-empty internal acknowledgement for the NO path. A hidden run that only performed intermediate tools and then completed empty now throws `ServiceUnavailableException`, emits `scheduled_assistant_action_dispatch_failed` with a `toolInvocationsSummary`, and re-enters the scheduler retry path instead of silently disappearing as a false success. **Tests.** `apps/api/test/send-native-web-chat-turn.service.test.ts` now pins `toolInvocations` passthrough, and `apps/api/test/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.test.ts` adds regressions for both the valid reminder-create terminal path and the previously-broken `web_search -> empty completion` path.

## Unreleased

### Added

- **Media tool fallback model routing in Admin Plans (`apps/api`, `apps/runtime`, `apps/web`, `packages/contracts`):** admin plans now expose per-tool primary + fallback model keys for `image_generate`, `image_edit`, and `video_generate`. Materialization writes those fallback choices into runtime tool credential refs, and runtime media execution now resolves a capability-aware model chain before calling the provider. The first active rule is transparent-background safety for image tools: requests using `background="transparent"` now auto-switch away from `gpt-image-2` when a compatible fallback is configured, or return a soft skipped tool result instead of bubbling a provider 400/500 path. Contracts, plan editor UI, generated client types, and focused runtime/admin tests were updated together.

- **Transparent background support for image tools (`apps/runtime`, `apps/provider-gateway`):** `image_generate` and `image_edit` now expose a first-class `background` option (`auto` / `transparent` / `opaque`) in the runtime contract and model-visible tool schemas. The OpenAI Images payload forwards it for both generate and edit while keeping `output_format: "png"` so transparent requests can preserve alpha. Tool catalog guidance now tells the model to set `background="transparent"` for cutouts, stickers, icons, logos, background removal, or PNG-with-alpha requests.

- **Durable assistant notification outbox and idle reengagement (`apps/api` + `/admin/notifications`):** added `assistant_notification_outbox` plus `workspace_notification_policies`, `AssistantNotificationOutboxService`, and `AssistantNotificationOutboxSchedulerService` so reminders, background-task pushes, idle reengagement, and future system events share one durable retry/dead-letter/idempotency path before preferred-channel delivery. `HandleInternalCronFireService` and `PersaiBackgroundTaskSchedulerService` now enqueue instead of calling delivery directly; background-task runs store the outbox id and are updated with final delivery result by the worker. Added `PersaiIdleReengagementSchedulerService`, which uses admin-configured idle/cooldown policy and LLM instruction to evaluate a compact recent-context packet and enqueue one deduped idle notification when the evaluator returns `push`. `/admin/notifications` is now "Notification Settings": existing webhook/system channel controls remain, and a new user-notification policy section edits idle reengagement enablement, threshold, cooldown, and LLM instruction. Mobile push remains deferred; the delivery model is ready for a future adapter.

- **ADR-077 assistant background-task runtime foundation (`apps/api` schema + scheduler + runtime contract):** accepted the clean replacement architecture for assistant-side background work: `scheduled_action` stays for user-visible reminders only, while assistant quiet actions move to a new `background_task` runtime with direct preferred-channel push and first-class run history. The first code slices add `assistant_background_tasks` plus `assistant_background_task_runs`, internal background-task create/list/pause/resume/cancel APIs, the runtime `background_task` worker tool, runtime structured evaluator endpoint, API scheduler/claim/retry executor, preferred-channel push/no_push recording, tool-catalog/preset guidance cleanup, and runtime removal of new `assistant_check` creation through `scheduled_action`. The UI target remains the existing assistant settings cards: "Задачи для тебя" backed by reminders and "Действия ассистента" backed by background tasks plus expandable recent-run history. No legacy `assistant_check` compatibility is introduced in the target architecture.

- **Shared assistant notification delivery layer (`apps/api`; focused cron/delivery regression green):** added `AssistantNotificationDeliveryService` and common source/result types for `user_reminder`, `background_task`, `idle_reengagement`, and `system_event` notifications. The active path now reaches that delivery service through the durable outbox worker, with no reminder-specific wrapper left in the codebase; it preserves the existing preferred-channel semantics, Telegram-first delivery, web fallback to `system:notifications`, and `MediaDeliveryService` artifact persistence.

- **Password reveal control (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** custom auth password fields and profile password-change fields now have a calm eye toggle so users can verify what they typed. The shared `PasswordField` component keeps the reveal UI consistent across sign-in, sign-up, reset-password, and profile password forms.

- **Telegram settings system notes localization (`apps/web`; focused typecheck green):** the Telegram settings panel now maps the three API-provided architecture notes to localized RU/EN strings instead of rendering the raw English backend text under `System notes`. Unknown future notes still fall back to their server-provided text.

- **Web chat pre-response status polish — assistant now shows a quiet `Thinking...` / `Working...` cue before the first token (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** empty streaming assistant bubbles now render a subtle cursor plus localized pre-response label. If no tool activity is attached yet, the bubble says `Thinking...` / `Думаю...`; if the next live entry is an active `tool_use` badge, it says `Working...` / `Работаю...` while the concrete activity badge remains visible. The status disappears as soon as assistant text starts streaming, so no `Thought for N s` surface is introduced. Focused verification: `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/web exec vitest run app/app/_components/chat-message.test.tsx app/app/_components/chat-area.test.tsx`, `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/web run typecheck`, and targeted `prettier --check` are green.

- **ADR-074 Slice L1.1 — Cost-counting holes from live observation (founder live observation 2026-04-23 «я сказал сделай 3 картинки и он сделал, хотя per-turn cap=1»; conscious revision of the original L1 founder anchor; code-landed; verification gate green; awaiting `persai-dev` deploy):** the L1 ship left three cost-counting holes that all surfaced in the same founder turn — `image_generate.count: 1..4` advanced the per-turn cap by exactly 1 regardless of `count` (so cap=1 silently allowed 4 OpenAI-billed artifacts), six cost tools (`tts`, `browser`, `exec`, `shell`, `files`, `scheduled_action`) had **no** code default in `TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN` so a single iteration could fan out to dozens of parallel calls, and the daily-quota counter was a no-op when the plan had `dailyCallLimit: null` while three tools (`memory_write`, `knowledge_search`, `knowledge_fetch`) never called it at all — provider was billed but `tool_daily_usage` stayed at zero. **Caps + schema clamp.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/tool-budget-policy.ts:TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN` now ships founder-confirmed defaults for every cost tool (`tts:3`, `browser:3`, `exec:5`, `shell:5`, `files:10`, `scheduled_action:5`, `knowledge_search:5`, `knowledge_fetch:10`, `memory_write:10`); the last three are an **explicit revision** of the original L1 founder anchor that left memory/knowledge tools uncapped — the L1.1 spirit is preserved by setting _generous_ defaults (large enough for normal durable-memory loops, tight enough to block runaway fan-out), not zero. The shared-compaction tools (`summarize_context`, `compact_context`) remain absent because the runtime drives them at most once per turn. `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts:createImageGenerateToolDefinition` clamps the model-facing `count.maximum` to `min(MAX_RUNTIME_IMAGE_GENERATE_COUNT, effectivePerTurnCap)` via the new `resolveImageGenerateCountCap(policy)` helper, so cap=1 mechanically refuses `count > 1` at the model boundary; the description now also tells the model that each requested image consumes one cap unit and one daily-quota unit. **API contract: `units` weight.** `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/domain/workspace-tool-daily-usage.repository.ts:WorkspaceToolDailyUsageRepository` adds an optional `units` parameter (default 1) on both `incrementAndGet` and `consumeWithinLimit`. The Prisma implementation (`prisma-workspace-tool-daily-usage.repository.ts`) defensively normalises `units` to a positive integer (`normalizeUnits`) so a buggy caller cannot zero or reverse the counter, and `consumeWithinLimitTx` rejects the _whole_ batch when `currentCount + units > dailyCallLimit` (no partial commits). `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/track-workspace-quota-usage.service.ts:consumeToolDailyLimit` accepts `units?: number` and `dailyCallLimit: number | null` — when the plan has no daily cap it now falls through to `incrementAndGet` for observability and returns `limit: null` instead of short-circuiting. `consume-internal-runtime-tool-daily-limit.service.ts:parseInput` accepts a nullable `dailyCallLimit` (the runtime forwards what its bundle saw, the API re-resolves the live plan as the source of truth) and a positive-integer `units` (defaults to 1 for older runtime workers; non-positive integers are rejected with `BadRequestException`). The interface controller `internal-runtime-tool-quota.controller.ts` now declares `Promise<{ ok; currentCount; limit: number | null }>`. **Runtime: always count.** Every cost-tool service drops the prior `if (policy.dailyCallLimit !== null)` guard so it always pings the consume endpoint — `runtime-image-generate-tool.service.ts` now passes `units: request.count`; `runtime-tts-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-browser-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-video-generate-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-image-edit-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-files-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-sandbox-tool.service.ts`, `runtime-scheduled-action-tool.service.ts`, plus the `web_search` and `web_fetch` paths in `turn-execution.service.ts` all forward the bundle's observed `dailyCallLimit` (which may be null). The runtime client `persai-internal-api.client.service.ts:consumeToolDailyLimit` widens its type to `dailyCallLimit: number | null` and adds an optional `units?: number`; `ConsumeToolDailyLimitOutcome.allowed=true` now also has `limit: number | null` to model the always-count-no-enforcement branch. **Runtime: missing-quota fixes.** `runtime-knowledge-tool.service.ts` adds a small `consumeQuota(bundle, toolCode)` helper that resolves the local policy and pings the API for both `executeSearchToolCall` and `executeFetchToolCall`; `runtime-memory-write-tool.service.ts:executeToolCall` does the same up front for `memory_write`. Both honour the founder anchor by silently skipping when the assistant has no policy entry for the tool (the orchestrator would already have refused to dispatch the call). **Admin UI.** `apps/web/app/admin/plans/page.tsx` replaces the misleading "Blank daily cap means this tool inherits the plan default behavior" with "Blank daily cap = no daily limit (calls are still counted for observability but never refused). Set a positive integer to enforce a hard daily ceiling per workspace; the call is rejected once the counter reaches it." and extends the `Per-turn cap` helptext with the full L1.1 defaults table so an admin can see at a glance which tools have a code default and what the value is. **Tests.** `apps/runtime/test/tool-budget-policy.test.ts` now asserts the L1.1 defaults for every newly-capped tool (with failure messages naming the L1.1 revision), keeps the L1 anchor for `compact_context`/`summarize_context` remaining uncapped, and pins `perToolCap("memory_write") === 10` / `perToolCap("knowledge_search") === 5` / `perToolCap("never_seen_tool") === null` directly. `apps/api/test/prisma-workspace-tool-daily-usage.repository.test.ts` adds two new tests covering weighted `consumeWithinLimit` (counter jumps by `units`, whole-batch denial when `current + units > cap`, defensive normalisation of zero/negative `units`) and weighted `incrementAndGet` (forwards `units` into the upsert, default `units=1` keeps older callers wire-compatible). `apps/api/test/consume-internal-runtime-tool-daily-limit.service.test.ts` adds: parsing accepts an absent `units` (treated as 1) and a null `dailyCallLimit`; `image_generate`-style weighted call (`units=4`) is forwarded verbatim; null-cap plan still succeeds and returns `limit: null` (always-count); deactivated tool remains a hard rejection (only blocking path left); `units=0` and negative values are rejected with `BadRequestException`. The runtime fakes in `runtime-tts-tool.service.test.ts`, `runtime-video-generate-tool.service.test.ts`, `turn-execution.service.test.ts`, `runtime-knowledge-tool.service.test.ts`, `runtime-memory-write-tool.service.test.ts`, and `runtime-scheduled-action-tool.service.test.ts` widen their mock `consumeToolDailyLimit` signatures to `dailyCallLimit: number | null` + optional `units`, and the previously-quota-less fakes (memory/knowledge/scheduled*action) gain a `consumeToolDailyLimit` mock returning `{ allowed: true, currentCount, limit: null }`. The `image_generate` integration assertion in `turn-execution.service.test.ts` now expects `units: 1` on the recorded consume call. **Out of scope (deliberate, deferred to follow-ups).** R1 plurality detection / `requestedBudget`, R2 true wall-clock parallelism, R3 compound tools all remain explicitly out of scope. This slice does not change cap \_values* on any existing plan — operators keep whatever daily caps they already configured; L1.1 only fixes the _measurement_ layer so caps and counters now match what providers actually bill. No Prisma migration was needed (the new columns/contracts are all additive on the wire and the DB row layout is unchanged). The ADR-074 § L1.1 section explicitly flags the memory/knowledge cap as a conscious revision of the L1 founder anchor so a future reader does not misread it as silent.

- **ADR-074 Slice L1 turnkey closeout — API-side bundle compile + admin PATCH + admin UI for the L1 tool-loop budgets (founder Q9-C closeout; code-landed; verification gate green):** the previous L1 follow-up entry shipped only the runtime read for the `runtime.toolBudgets` and `RuntimeToolPolicy.perTurnCap` overrides; every published bundle still arrived with both fields absent because the API-side compile pipeline did not know how to populate them. This change closes the loop end-to-end so the founder can edit the per-mode loop limits and the per-tool hard caps directly from `/admin/plans` without a runtime release. **Schema.** New nullable `Int?` column `per_turn_cap` on `plan_catalog_tool_activations` via reversible additive migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260423030000_adr074_l1_plan_per_turn_cap/migration.sql` (NULL means "fall back to runtime code default", `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER` means "uncap on this plan"); the per-mode loop-limit overrides reuse the existing `PlanCatalogPlan.billingProviderHints` JSON column under a versioned `toolBudgets` block (`{ schema: "persai.toolBudgets.v1", loopLimitByMode: { normal, premium, reasoning } }`) so no new column or migration was needed for them. `AssistantPlanCatalogToolActivation` (domain) and `AssistantPlanCatalogToolActivationOverride` (repo write input) gain a non-optional `perTurnCap: number | null` field; the Prisma repository `mapToDomain` and `syncToolActivationsForPlan` carry the column through the upsert. **API parser / serializer.** New helper `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/tool-budgets-policy.ts` mirrors the `context-hydration-policy.ts` shape with `createDefaultPlanToolBudgets` / `parsePlanToolBudgets` (strict — rejects 0 / negative / fractional / non-numeric per leaf with `BadRequestException`) / `resolveStoredPlanToolBudgets` (lenient — garbage degrades to NULL so an old/garbage row never blocks compile) / `toPlanToolBudgetsDocument` (emits the schema marker) / `hasAnyToolBudgetOverride` (used to skip emitting an empty `toolBudgets` block when every leaf is NULL). `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/admin-plan-management.types.ts` gains `AdminPlanToolBudgets` plus `perTurnCap: number | null` on both `AdminPlanToolActivation` and `AdminPlanToolActivationInput`; `AdminPlanInput` and `AdminPlanState` carry the new `toolBudgets: AdminPlanToolBudgets` field. `ManageAdminPlansService.parsePlanInput` reads `parsed.toolBudgets` through `parsePlanToolBudgets`, `parseToolActivations` validates `typed.perTurnCap` as a positive integer or null, `toWriteInput` only emits the `toolBudgets` JSON block when `hasAnyToolBudgetOverride` is true (keeping bundle JSON minimal for the common case), `toCanonicalToolActivationOverrides` propagates `perTurnCap` into the repo write, and `toAdminPlanState` round-trips both fields back via `resolveStoredPlanToolBudgets`. **Bundle compile.** `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/runtime-tool-policy.ts:ToolQuotaPolicyEntry` gains `perTurnCap: number | null`; `resolveRuntimeToolPolicies` builds a `perTurnCapByCode` map (mirroring `dailyLimitByCode`) and stamps the value onto every `RuntimeToolPolicy` it constructs (synthetic system tools and hidden-internal tools always emit `perTurnCap: null` so they fall back to the code default). `MaterializeAssistantPublishedVersionService.resolveToolQuotaPolicy` now selects `perTurnCap` from `prisma.planCatalogToolActivation` and forwards it; new private `resolvePlanToolBudgets(planCode)` reads `PlanCatalogPlan.billingProviderHints.toolBudgets.loopLimitByMode`, sanitizes each leaf (positive integers only, anything else collapses to NULL), and `buildRuntimeArtifacts` only injects `runtime.toolBudgets: { loopLimitByMode }` into the compile input when at least one leaf is non-null (`hasAnyLoopOverride`) — preserving compact bundle JSON for the common case. **Warm-path validation.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/bundles/runtime-bundle-registry.service.ts:assertValidToolPolicy` now rejects `perTurnCap` values that are neither null nor strictly-positive integers (`bundleDocument.governance.toolPolicies["<code>"].perTurnCap must be null, omitted, or a strictly-positive integer`); new `assertToolBudgetsConfig` rejects malformed `runtime.toolBudgets.loopLimitByMode.{normal,premium,reasoning}` with the same rule. So a misconfigured override caught here at warm-path-load aborts the bundle instead of silently falling back to the code default. **Seeding.** `apps/api/prisma/tool-catalog-data.ts:STARTER_TRIAL_TOOL_POLICY` gains an explicit `perTurnCap: number | null` field on every entry (every starter row is `null` so the seeded plan inherits the runtime defaults). `apps/api/prisma/seed.ts` and `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/seed-tool-catalog.service.ts` carry the column through their respective `planCatalogToolActivation.upsert` calls so re-seeding a fresh DB writes `per_turn_cap = NULL` instead of leaving the column unset. **Public API contract.** `packages/contracts/openapi.yaml` adds `perTurnCap` (nullable integer with prose) to `AdminPlanToolActivation` and `AdminPlanToolActivationInput` and a new `AdminPlanToolBudgets` schema (`{ loopLimitByMode: { normal, premium, reasoning } }`, all nullable integers) referenced from `AdminPlanState` / `AdminPlanInputBase`. The orval client was regenerated (`pnpm --filter @persai/contracts run generate`); the regenerated `packages/contracts/src/generated/**` is checked in and prettier-formatted. **Admin UI.** `apps/web/app/admin/plans/page.tsx` gains a new "Per-turn cap" input next to the existing "Daily cap" on every editable tool row in `ToolActivationsEdit` (with `setPerTurnCap` mirroring `setLimit`, blank means "use code default"), and a new `Sec` panel "Tool budgets (loop limits per execution mode)" with three integer inputs for `normal` / `premium` / `reasoning` plus help text explaining the resolution order. `ToolActivationDraft` and `PlanDraft` are extended accordingly; `planToDraft` populates them defensively from `AdminPlanState.toolBudgets.loopLimitByMode` (falling back to "" when null), `draftToPayload` parses each blank → `null` and each filled value through `parseStrictIntegerDraft` so a 0 / negative is caught at submit-time on the client. The page test fixture (`page.test.tsx`) now seeds `perTurnCap: null` and a defaulted `toolBudgets` block. **Tests.** New `apps/api/test/tool-budgets-policy.test.ts` exhaustively covers default + parser + resolver paths (round-trip schema marker, all-null = no-override, partial overrides survive, strict parser rejects 0 / -1 / 1.5 / NaN / "5" / true with `BadRequestException`, lenient resolver always returns defaults for garbage and keeps valid leaves while degrading bad ones to null). `apps/api/test/manage-admin-plans.service.test.ts` extended with a Slice L1 block that asserts `parseUpdateInput` carries `perTurnCap` through, `toWriteInput` writes the `persai.toolBudgets.v1` block to `billingProviderHints` only when there is an override, the override is omitted from `billingProviderHints` when every loop limit is null, strict parser rejects non-positive `perTurnCap` and non-positive loop limits with the right field path in the error, and `toAdminPlanState` round-trips both `toolBudgets` and per-tool `perTurnCap` from on-disk billingHints back to the admin DTO. `apps/api/test/runtime-tool-policy.test.ts` adds `perTurnCap` to its `planToolQuotaPolicy` fixture and asserts the runtime tool policy carries it for `web_search` (= 2), keeps `null` for `image_generate` (no override), and keeps `null` for synthetic (`compact_context`) and hidden-internal (`cron`) policies. `apps/runtime/test/runtime-bundle-registry.service.test.ts` adds two new fixtures + assertions: misconfigured `perTurnCap = 0` on a tool policy is rejected (`/perTurnCap must be null, omitted, or a strictly-positive integer/`), and misconfigured `toolBudgets.loopLimitByMode.normal = 0` is rejected (`/toolBudgets\.loopLimitByMode\.normal must be null or a strictly-positive integer/`). Verification gate: `pnpm lint` clean, `pnpm format:check` clean (after re-formatting the regenerated orval output), `pnpm typecheck` clean across all 14 workspace projects, `pnpm --filter @persai/api test` green, `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test` green, `pnpm --filter @persai/web test` green (19 files, 92 tests). **Out of scope.** This closeout intentionally does not introduce a Prisma migration that backfills existing `plan_catalog_tool_activations` rows — the new column defaults to NULL on every legacy row so behaviour is byte-for-byte identical pre-deploy until an admin actually saves a per-turn cap from the UI. R1 / R2 / R3 (model-supplied per-call budget hints, parallel tool dispatch, compound tools) remain explicitly out of scope. The ADR-074 L1 Status block is updated to record this closeout and supersede the prior "deferred to follow-up" wording.

- **ADR-074 Slice L1 follow-up — tool-loop budgets are now tunable per assistant via the runtime bundle (founder Q9-C revision; code-landed; verification gate green):** the original L1 prompt asked for the limits to be hard-coded constants, but the founder pushed back the same evening — «Числа подобраны под текущие модели (gpt-5.4, claude и т.д.) - я их меняю. Нельзя хардкодить эти лимиты это тупо» — because different plans ship different models and the loop/per-tool budgets have to travel with the model/plan, not be baked into runtime code. This change keeps the existing L1 numbers as code defaults but adds two override surfaces so the API-side bundle compile pipeline (and a future admin UI) can change them per assistant without a runtime release. **Contract changes.** `packages/runtime-contract/src/index.ts` gains a new `RuntimeToolBudgetsConfig` interface (`{ loopLimitByMode: { normal, premium, reasoning } | null }`) and a new optional field `perTurnCap?: number | null` on `RuntimeToolPolicy` (sitting next to the existing `dailyCallLimit`). `packages/runtime-bundle/src/index.ts` exposes both: `AssistantRuntimeBundleRuntimeConfig.toolBudgets?: RuntimeToolBudgetsConfig | null` and the existing `AssistantRuntimeBundleToolPolicy = RuntimeToolPolicy` re-export now carries the new `perTurnCap` field automatically. Both fields are optional, so every existing bundle on disk and in production keeps validating without migration. **Runtime read.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/tool-budget-policy.ts` now resolves the loop limit through `bundle.runtime.toolBudgets?.loopLimitByMode?.[mode] → TOOL_LOOP_LIMIT_BY_MODE[mode]` and the per-tool cap through `RuntimeToolPolicy.perTurnCap → TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN[toolCode] → null` (uncapped). The `ToolBudgetPolicy` constructor takes a new `options: { loopLimitOverrides?, perToolCapOverrides? }` bag; `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-execution.service.ts:createToolBudgetPolicy(execution)` now reads both from the bundle and the policy list (`collectPerToolCapOverrides(execution)` walks `bundle.governance.toolPolicies` and short-circuits to `null` when no policies set an override, so the hot path stays cheap). A defensive guard rejects `null` / `0` / negative overrides — a misconfigured bundle cannot accidentally turn the loop off (`loopLimit=0` would silently break every tool-using turn); to genuinely "uncap" a normally-capped tool the bundle must set `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER` (documented sentinel in the policy module). New exported helper `resolveAdvertisedPerTurnCap(toolName, overrides)` is consumed by the projection layer so model-facing tool descriptions show the cap that will actually fire at runtime, not the bare code default. **Projection update.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts` replaces every inline `TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN[name]` read inside the `web_search` / `web_fetch` / `image_generate` / `image_edit` / `video_generate` factories with a small `appendPerTurnCapHint(base, toolCode, policy)` / `describePerTurnCap(toolCode, policy)` helper pair that consults `policy.perTurnCap` first; tools whose effective cap is `null` (e.g. when a bundle uncapped them via `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER`) now correctly omit the suffix instead of advertising a stale number. **Tests.** `apps/runtime/test/tool-budget-policy.test.ts` gains override-path scenarios: bundle override `loopLimitByMode.normal=5` replaces the default of 2, `null` / `0` / `-3` overrides are ignored, per-tool override on `web_fetch` lifts the cap to 10 and 10 reservations succeed before exhaustion at 11, per-tool override can _add_ a cap to a normally-uncapped `knowledge_search` (`perTurnCap=2` exhausts on the 3rd call), and `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER` override on `image_generate` makes 50 calls succeed without per-tool exhaustion. `apps/runtime/test/turn-execution.service.test.ts` gains a 4th L1 integration scenario (`L1 Test 4 — per-assistant bundle override of loopLimitByMode`) that mutates `bundleRegistry.entry.parsedBundle.runtime.toolBudgets` to `{ loopLimitByMode: { normal: 5, premium: null, reasoning: null } }`, runs a normal-mode turn that emits 6 sequential `web_fetch` iterations, and asserts exactly 5 real `web_fetch` executions plus a synthesized `tool_budget_exhausted` toolHistory entry with `budgetReason: "loop_limit"`, `limit: 5`, `observed: 6`. The test resets `toolBudgets = null` in a `finally` so the override does not leak into later blocks. Verification gate: `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean, `pnpm format:check` clean, `pnpm -w typecheck` clean (runtime-contract / runtime-bundle / runtime / api / web all compile against the new optional fields without touching anything else), full `apps/runtime` suite green via `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test`, with the test log now showing four L1 `[tool-budget-exhausted]` WARN lines including the new override-driven `reason=loop_limit limit=5 observed=6 iteration=5` — proving the bundle override actually replaced the code default at runtime. **Out of scope (deferred).** This slice only adds the contract and the runtime read for the override fields. The bundle compiler in `apps/api` does **not** yet populate `runtime.toolBudgets` or `RuntimeToolPolicy.perTurnCap`, no admin UI exists for editing them, and there is no Prisma migration in this slice (both fields are optional). Until the API-side compile pipeline learns to populate them, every published bundle has both fields absent and the runtime falls back to the unchanged code defaults — so production behaviour after this deploy is byte-for-byte identical to the pre-revision L1 landing. R1 / R2 / R3 (model-supplied per-call budget hints, parallel tool dispatch, compound tools) remain explicitly out of scope. The ADR-074 wording that called the limits "not user-tunable" is superseded by this change; the L1 Status block in `docs/ADR/074-humanity-and-cost-polish-program.md` records the founder revision and the new resolution order so a future reader does not interpret the old wording as authoritative.

- **ADR-074 Slice L1 — Adaptive tool loop limits per execution mode (code-landed in code; verification gate green, awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live UI gates):** the runtime's native tool loop is no longer governed by the universal pre-L1 cap of `MAX_NATIVE_TOOL_LOOP_ITERATIONS = 4` that would fail any tool-heavy turn with `native_tool_loop_exhausted`; instead, every per-turn execution now constructs a `ToolBudgetPolicy` (new file `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/tool-budget-policy.ts`) seeded from the routing decision's `executionMode`, with founder-confirmed (Q9-C part 1) loop limits `TOOL_LOOP_LIMIT_BY_MODE = { normal: 2, premium: 4, reasoning: 8 }` plus per-turn hard caps `TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN = { web_fetch: 5, web_search: 3, image_generate: 1, image_edit: 1, video_generate: 1 }` (memory*\*, summarize_context, compact_context, knowledge*\* are intentionally absent so durable-memory work is never choked off by browse/media caps). Wiring sits in both the streaming branch (`streamAcceptedTurn` in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-execution.service.ts`, around the `for (const toolCall of event.result.toolCalls)` loop) and the non-streaming branch (`executeProviderToolLoop` in the same file): each emitted tool call now goes through `toolBudgetPolicy.reserve(toolCall.name, iteration)` before any external execution, and on `exhausted: true` the runtime substitutes the call with a structured `tool_budget_exhausted` outcome (created by `createToolBudgetExhaustedResult` in the new policy module — fields `toolCode`, `action: "skipped"`, `reason: "tool_budget_exhausted"`, `budgetReason: "loop_limit" | "per_tool_cap"`, `limit`, `observed`, plus a hint string that names the tool when the per-tool cap fires). The synthetic outcome flows through the same `applyToolExecutionOutcome` / `toolHistory` pipeline as a real tool result so the model sees it on the next provider iteration and is expected to wrap up with an honest user-facing reply ("I hit my budget for X — here is what I have so far"). The iteration cap itself is now `loopLimit() + NATIVE_TOOL_LOOP_WRAP_UP_ITERATIONS` (with `NATIVE_TOOL_LOOP_WRAP_UP_ITERATIONS = 2` reserving room for substituted-result delivery + final text reply); the `native_tool_loop_exhausted` failure message now reads `Native tool loop exceeded N iterations (mode=<mode>, loopLimit=<n>, wrapUp=2).` so live operators can tell at a glance which mode tripped the absolute ceiling. Each substitution emits a WARN line (`[tool-budget-exhausted] requestId=… sessionId=… tool=… reason=… limit=… observed=… iteration=…`) and a trace stage (`iter<n>.tool_budget_exhausted.<tool>`) so the S0 smoke harness and live `gcloud logging read` greps can detect exhaustion without parsing tool result bodies. The model-facing tool descriptions in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts` now suffix the per-turn cap inline (`web_search` / `web_fetch` / `image_generate` / `image_edit` / `video_generate`) by importing `TOOL_HARD_CAP_PER_TURN` from the new policy module, so the cap stays DRY between runtime enforcement and the model's projected tool-list. **Tests.** New file `apps/runtime/test/tool-budget-policy.test.ts` (registered in `apps/runtime/test/run-suite.ts`) unit-tests every founder-confirmed numeric (loop limits per mode, per-tool caps, the deliberate absence of `memory_write` / `compact_context` / `summarize_context` from the cap table), the `loopLimit()` per-mode lookup, the per-tool counter's exhaust-then-don't-bump invariant (so the smoke harness does not over-count exhaustion attempts), the loop-limit branch's same don't-bump invariant on the per-tool counter, and the `createToolBudgetExhaustedResult` shape including the per-tool hint that names the tool. Three new integration scenarios appended to `apps/runtime/test/turn-execution.service.test.ts` exercise the wired pipeline end-to-end: (a) normal-mode loop limit — three sequential `web_fetch` iterations produce exactly two real `webFetchCalls` and a synthesized `tool_budget_exhausted` toolHistory entry with `budgetReason: "loop_limit"`, then the model wraps up; (b) per-tool cap inside a single iteration — six `web_fetch` calls in iteration 0 produce exactly five real executions and one synthesized entry with `budgetReason: "per_tool_cap"`, `limit: 5`, `observed: 6`; (c) premium mode (deepMode=true) allows four real executions before the loop budget fires — proves the per-mode lookup works and that premium did not silently fall back to normal=2. Each assertion's failure message names the L1 bug class so a future regression points straight at the right slice. Verification gate: `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean, `pnpm format:check` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime run typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/api typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/web typecheck` clean, full `apps/runtime` suite green via `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime exec tsx test/run-suite.ts` with all three `[tool-budget-exhausted]` WARN lines visible (`reason=loop_limit limit=2 observed=3 iteration=2`, `reason=per_tool_cap limit=5 observed=6 iteration=0`, `reason=loop_limit limit=4 observed=5 iteration=4`). **Out of scope** (deferred to R1/R2/R3 per the slice spec): per-tool-call requested-budget hints from the model, parallel tool-call dispatch within an iteration, compound/reusable tools, and any change to the routing decision itself — L1 only consumes the existing `executionMode` and never re-routes. Awaiting `persai-dev` deploy and the four founder live UI gates listed in the L1 acceptance section of `docs/ADR/074-humanity-and-cost-polish-program.md` (chitchat-short still ≤1 tool call, tool-heavy-search completes within new limits, exhaustion shows up in trace output, no `native_tool_loop_exhausted` failures on tool-heavy scenarios).

### Changed

- **Desktop chat jump-to-latest placement (`apps/web`; focused test/typecheck green):** on desktop web, the `↓ К последним` floating pill now sits centered above the composer instead of hiding near the right edge. Mobile keeps the existing placement.

- **Landing CTA simplification (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** the welcome hero now has one dominant primary CTA, while `Plans` and `Sign in` are quiet same-weight text links. This removes the three-different-buttons feel and keeps the public gateway more minimal and premium.

- **Telegram settings simplification + Markdown default (`apps/api` + `apps/web`; focused tests/typechecks green):** new Telegram bot connections now default to `Markdown` parse mode instead of plain text, so formatted replies work out of the box. The Telegram settings panel copy was shortened and de-noised, with less explanatory text in the central config block. The public welcome center copy was shortened further, while the footer returned to the smaller quiet style.

- **Public welcome screen noise reduction (`apps/web`; focused typecheck green):** the central hero area is quieter: the three capability cards became a single low-contrast inline capability line, platform pills were visually softened, and the footer links now sit in a clearer compact footer rail with better contrast. The page stays one-screen and keeps the existing CTA hierarchy.

### Fixed

- **Web chat continuity hotfix (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** fixed a severe active-turn/history merge bug where restored streaming assistant placeholders with server ids could survive next to committed final answers, producing phantom cursors and duplicated/mixed chat history after reload or chat switching. `loadHistory()`, active refresh, and terminal reconciliation now remove the full active snapshot message set before appending committed messages instead of naively merging live placeholders into server history; replacement now requires an assistant message after the active user in returned history, so older assistant messages cannot prematurely clear a still-running cursor/tool status. Restore polling timers are no longer cleared on resume-listener re-renders, and chat scroll anchoring now resets on chat changes and scrolls the actual overflow container to the bottom.

- **Web chat desktop/mobile continuity hardening (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** active turn storage is now cleared on attachment staging and pre-header send failures so reload cannot restore phantom turns. Retrying a failed send now follows an already accepted/running server turn with bounded turn-status polling instead of getting stuck in `reconciling`. Soft-detach reconciliation no longer treats an unrelated last-20 history tail as proof that the current turn completed; it validates the active server user message and falls back to `clientTurnId` turn status for long chats. Normal sends remap optimistic user bubbles to the authoritative server user id, welcome turns share the active-turn restore path, and bare `/app/chat` keeps a stable draft thread key across remounts until the server chat is created and mirrored into the URL.

- **Notification Settings auth + empty-state polish (`apps/api` + `apps/web`):** fixed the new idle-reengagement policy endpoints missing from `ClerkAuthMiddleware`, which made `/admin/notifications` show a false `Session expired` banner on a valid session. The middleware registration is pinned by `identity-access.module.test.ts`. The page now renders a real inactive webhook card even before any webhook row exists and uses a more polished admin layout for the durable outbox/user-notification policy surface.

- **Web-search post-tool stream finalization (`apps/api`; focused watchdog regression green):** the web-chat cadence watchdog no longer starts the 8s silent timer immediately after a native tool finishes. Live GKE logs showed a `web_search` turn where the OpenAI follow-up stream was aborted about 8s after tool completion before the model emitted its first final-answer event, even though OpenAI later showed the answer had been generated. Tool execution is still protected by in-flight suspension, and normal provider/runtime stream timeouts remain the guard for true hangs; the watchdog now resumes only after the next post-tool activity/delta. Focused verification: `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/api exec tsx test/cadence-watchdog.test.ts`.

- **Background-completed chat stream restore (`apps/web`; focused regression green):** when a long web chat turn finishes while its thread is not the active chat, the completed optimistic user/assistant pair is now committed into the per-thread in-memory history cache before the live snapshot is cleared. Returning to that chat immediately restores the sent message and final answer instead of showing an empty thread until refresh/history refetch catches up. Focused verification: `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/web exec vitest run app/app/_components/use-chat.test.tsx`.

- **Chat attachment upload navigation resilience (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** large chat attachment staging no longer applies an absolute client-side hard timeout to chat attachments, avoiding slow-but-progressing PDF/photo uploads failing just because the wall clock passed 5 minutes, and pairs with the per-thread pending-send state so switching away no longer loses the originating chat's pending/failed attachment message. Sidebar chat switching now uses local History API URL updates instead of `router.push`, so changing chats does not wait for an App Router/RSC navigation request that can be delayed while a large upload is in flight. Loaded chat histories are now cached in memory per thread/chat and restored immediately on return, avoiding a fresh history fetch for already visited chats while another upload is saturating the connection. Attachment staging uses XHR progress again, but without hard/stall upload timeouts, so pending file/media cards can show compact upload percentages without reintroducing timer-based false failures. Attachment sends no longer show the duplicate off-bubble spinner on the right; the in-card pending indicator remains the single upload cue. The chat composer textarea now explicitly disables manual resize so the global textarea handle does not appear in the main chat input; autosize and max-height scrolling remain unchanged.
- **Runtime tool-loop empty finalization hardening (`apps/runtime`; focused tests/typecheck green):** streaming and non-streaming native turn execution now detect the pathological provider/model case where a tool has already executed successfully but the tool-loop follow-up returns `completed` with no visible assistant text. Instead of letting that become an empty assistant output that surfaces in web chat as a broken/incomplete stream, runtime performs one safe final-text-only follow-up pass with tools disabled and an explicit developer instruction to finish the user-visible answer from the already-provided tool results.
- **Clerk avatar test cleanup (`apps/web`; full web suite green):** the Clerk avatar hook now tolerates an undefined Clerk test return value and suppresses late reload state updates after unmount, and its test explicitly flushes/cleans up the reload microtask. This fixes the CI-only unhandled `useUser()`/`window is not defined` failure in the full web test suite.

- **Admin presets reset-to-default reliability (`apps/api` + `apps/web`; focused tests/typechecks green):** prompt-template reset now uses an API-backed factory-default endpoint instead of a stale frontend copy of defaults, and the content-editable editor immediately refreshes its local text after reset. This fixes `/admin/presets` resets appearing to do nothing from the top prompt blocks through the tool prompt area.

- **Admin presets use-code-default persistence (`apps/api`; focused tests/typecheck green):** the tool catalog boot sync no longer writes code-default model descriptions/guidance into `providerHints` as manual overrides. Explicit `null` / use-code-default choices now survive API deploy/reseed, legacy rows that stored the exact code default are normalized back to `null`, and real custom overrides are preserved.

- **Telegram owner-claim return sync + mobile mic short-tap visual polish (`apps/web`; focused tests/typecheck green):** the Telegram settings panel now performs a narrow, event-driven refresh after the user explicitly taps `Find bot` and returns from Telegram, with one delayed follow-up check to catch claim propagation. This avoids a global app focus refresh while removing the need for a manual page reload after owner claim. The mobile voice button no longer ships desktop `hover:*` styling on touch devices and blurs after pointer-up/cancel, preventing the mic icon from staying visually hovered after a short tap. Focused verification: `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/web exec vitest run app/app/_components/chat-input.test.tsx`, `corepack pnpm --filter @persai/web run typecheck`, targeted `prettier --check`.

- **Background scheduled-action contract hardening — explicit `kind="user_reminder"` vs `kind="assistant_check"` replaces the old audience-coercion heuristic (founder repro on `persai-dev`: conditional background tasks like "если через 2 минуты я не напишу \"космос\", пингани меня" were silently collapsing into ordinary reminders with dumb instruction-text pushes):** the previous F2 safeguard solved one production fire but encoded the wrong long-term truth: `scheduled_action.create` still used one overloaded shape (`audience="user"` / `audience="assistant"`), `actionPayload` was only conditionally validated, and the backend tried to "help" by coercing malformed assistant creates into user reminders. That fixed unconditional "пни меня через 2 минуты" but broke honest conditional checks — the model could promise "я сейчас задам actionPayload", still emit an empty assistant create, and the backend would silently rewrite it into a user reminder whose `reminderText` was often the raw condition text (`If in 2 minutes the user has not written...`). **Fix:** `scheduled_action.create` is now a strict discriminated contract. `kind="user_reminder"` requires `title` + `reminderText` + exactly one schedule and rejects `actionType` / `actionPayload`. `kind="assistant_check"` requires `title` + `actionType` + a NON-EMPTY `actionPayload` + exactly one schedule and rejects `reminderText`. The runtime-facing schema in `packages/runtime-contract/src/index.ts` is now a real union, the model-visible tool schema in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts` advertises `kind` instead of `audience`, and the runtime parser in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/runtime-scheduled-action-tool.service.ts` rejects legacy `audience=` create calls up front with structured `invalid_arguments` tool errors. `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/persai-internal-api.client.service.ts` and `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/control-internal-scheduled-action.service.ts` were updated in lock-step so the API derives storage `audience` from `kind` and no longer does **any** routing coercion or `coercedFromAudience` response shaping. `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.ts` now treats assistant-side scheduled turns as a strict `assistant_check` executor path only: malformed legacy rows with null/empty payload are rejected loudly instead of being papered over, and the prompt tells the model to emit `kind="user_reminder"` on match or `kind="assistant_check"` for the next recheck. `apps/api/prisma/tool-catalog-data.ts` guidance was rewritten to explain the two explicit modes and to forbid instruction-like `reminderText` for user-visible pushes. `apps/api/prisma/bootstrap-preset-data.ts` heartbeat guidance was aligned to `kind="user_reminder"`. **Tests:** `apps/api/test/control-internal-scheduled-action.service.test.ts` now pins the strict contract (`assistant_check` requires non-empty payload; `user_reminder` rejects hidden fields) and removes the old coercion regression. `apps/api/test/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.test.ts` now expects the executor prompt to speak in `kind="user_reminder"` / `kind="assistant_check"` terms and to reject malformed null-payload assistant rows. `apps/runtime/test/runtime-scheduled-action-tool.service.test.ts` and `apps/runtime/test/turn-execution.service.test.ts` were updated to exercise the new `kind` contract end-to-end. **Why this is the real fix:** conditional background tasks can no longer silently degrade into ordinary reminders, and unconditional reminders can no longer leak technical instruction text to the user — the tool contract itself now encodes the product truth instead of relying on backend guessing.

- **Background scheduled-action stack v2 — empty-completion safety + audience routing-coercion + executor-style assistant prompt + duplicate-guard removal (founder repro continued: «время вышло ничего не произошло иди ищи причину в log и устраняй надоело уже»; second FIX bundle on top of the F1 entry below, again deliberately not modelled as a new ADR slice):** after the F1 fixes deployed to `persai-dev`, a fresh founder repro («поставь себе задачу пнуть меня через 2 минуты чтобы твоя фоновая задача сработала») still ended without a push. Tracing taskId `fc23766c-…` through GKE between `2026-04-23T11:56:55Z` and `2026-04-23T12:04:39Z` showed the new structured retry/dead-letter contract worked exactly as designed — but the failures it was retrying came from `Provider gateway request failed with status 500.`, attempt 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 → `task_disabled_after_exhausted_retries`. OpenAI logs (UI screenshots from the founder) showed the model legitimately calling `scheduled_action({"action":"list", "audience":"assistant"})` and then producing **no output** — no text, no tool call. Root-causing across `provider-gateway` + `runtime` + `api` revealed three interlocking issues that all needed to land together:

  **(F2-a) Provider gateway treated empty completions as a 500.** `apps/provider-gateway/src/modules/providers/openai/openai-provider.client.ts:generateText` threw `Error("OpenAI provider response did not contain text output.")` when the model returned no text and no tool calls; `streamText` yielded a `failed` event for the same shape. `apps/provider-gateway/src/modules/providers/anthropic/anthropic-provider.client.ts` had the symmetric throw / failed-event pair. But "no text + no tool calls" is a legitimate end-of-turn for our proactive prompts (`"Prefer silence over guessing"`) and for any assistant-side check turn that decides nothing needs to happen — so a single such turn was cascading into 500 → scheduler retry → 500 → … → dead-letter, with **zero** observable signal pre-F1. Fix: both clients now return `text: null, stopReason: "completed", toolCalls: []` for that shape and emit one structured warn (`openai_empty_completion` / `anthropic_empty_completion`) carrying enough diagnostics to spot pathological patterns (`outputItemTypes`, `outputItemCount`, `hasOutputText`, `finishReason`, `inputTokens`, `outputTokens`, `runtimeRequestId`, `transport: "stream"` on the streaming side). New helpers `summarizeOutputItemTypes` / `readNonStreamingFinishReason` / `readMetadataRequestId` in the OpenAI client and `summarizeAnthropicContentBlockTypes` in the Anthropic client keep the warn payload cheap. The existing `provider_invalid_response` failed events are still emitted for genuinely broken shapes (e.g. `stop_reason="tool_use"` with zero tool calls).

  **(F2-b) Runtime turn-execution treated `text === null` as a 500.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-execution.service.ts:buildTurnResult` threw `InternalServerErrorException` when the provider returned a completed turn with `text === null`. With the F2-a fix, that became reachable for the first time. Fix: `buildTurnResult` now materialises `assistantText: ""` (the chat surface simply doesn't render an empty bubble) and emits one warn — `Turn "<requestId>" finished as empty completion (provider=… model=…); rendering as empty assistant turn.` — so we can still spot pathological patterns in GKE without breaking the user-visible flow.

  **(F2-c) Routing-coercion for "set yourself a reminder" colloquialisms in `ControlInternalScheduledActionService.createScheduledAction`.** The deeper problem was that the model was creating `audience="assistant"` rows for what the user clearly meant as `audience="user"` ("поставь СЕБЕ задачу пнуть меня через 2 мин" reads literally as "set yourself a task" but semantically is just "ping me in 2 min"). The assistant-side check turn then had nothing to evaluate (empty `actionPayload`), so the model called `scheduled_action(action="list")` to orient itself, got an empty list, and went silent — the user never got the ping. Fix: a conservative heuristic `looksLikeUnconditionalAssistantTask(input)` returns true exactly when `input.actionPayload` is `undefined` or has zero keys, and `createScheduledAction` then transparently rewrites `audience="assistant" → "user"` (with `reminderText` resolved as `actionPayload?.reminderText ?? input.reminderText ?? input.title`, and `actionType` / `actionPayload` dropped), schedules the user-side row at the requested time, and surfaces `coercedFromAudience: "assistant"` in the response. The runtime tool layer (`apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/runtime-scheduled-action-tool.service.ts`) reads that field and surfaces a `warning` on the model-visible tool result (`Routed to audience="user" because actionPayload was empty. For unconditional reminders, call scheduled_action with audience="user" directly.`) so the model self-corrects on the next turn. Rows _with_ a non-empty `actionPayload` (any structured context the assistant-side turn could reason on) are left untouched — this only catches the colloquial-wording failure mode, not legitimate conditional probes. A structured `scheduled_action_coerced_to_user_push` log line records every coercion with `{ assistantId, title, originalActionType }`.

  **(F2-d) `buildScheduledActionPrompt` rewritten as an EXECUTOR brief.** `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.ts:buildScheduledActionPrompt` no longer uses the "decider" framing with `"Prefer silence over guessing"` — that line caused the model to interpret an empty payload as "nothing to do" and silently end the turn. The new prompt has two branches keyed on whether `actionPayload` is non-empty: WITH-payload turns must end with exactly one `scheduled_action(action="create", audience="user", delayMs=1, …)` (condition met) OR `scheduled_action(action="create", audience="assistant", actionType=<same>, actionPayload=<same>, runAt=<next-check>)` (condition not met, schedule next slot); WITHOUT-payload turns (which should not normally happen because F2-c routing-coercion prevents them, but if backed coercion didn't run for some reason) must immediately create an `audience="user"` push so the user actually receives something. Both branches forbid `scheduled_action(action="list")` (the actionPayload IS the brief, there is nothing to look up) and forbid creating another mirror `audience="assistant"` row without changing `runAt` (would cause an infinite-recheck loop). The header explicitly says `Silence is not a valid outcome.`

  **(F2-e) Removed the F1 `duplicate_audience_create_detected` soft guard** (`warnIfDuplicateAudienceCreate` in `ControlInternalScheduledActionService`) — once F2-c routing-coercion lands, every "пни меня через X" turn legitimately creates exactly one `audience="user"` row from a colloquial `audience="assistant"` request, and the F1 warn would have fired on every healthy coercion. The constants `DUPLICATE_AUDIENCE_CREATE_WINDOW_MS` and `normalizeTitleForDuplicateCheck` are gone with it. The `Nested assistant scheduled_action creation is not allowed` guard against recursion inside an already-running assistant-side check turn is preserved.

  **(F2-f) `scheduled_action.modelUsageGuidance` rewritten** in `apps/api/prisma/tool-catalog-data.ts` to give the model a clearer up-front picture: pick `audience="user"` for unconditional pings (the user WILL receive them), pick `audience="assistant"` only for genuine conditional rechecks where you provide a non-empty `actionPayload` describing what to evaluate, and ignore the colloquial "поставь себе" phrasing — pick the audience by SEMANTICS not wording. The text also explicitly tells the model that an empty `actionPayload` will be coerced to `audience="user"` server-side, so the model has a path to correct itself.

  **Tests.** New `apps/provider-gateway/test/openai-empty-completion.test.ts` and `apps/provider-gateway/test/anthropic-empty-completion.test.ts` each pin three scenarios: empty non-streaming completion → `text: null, stopReason: "completed"` + warn fires + no throw; tool calls still surface correctly with `stopReason: "tool_calls"`; empty streaming completion produces a single `completed` event with `text: null` (no `failed` event in the stream). Both are wired into `apps/provider-gateway/test/run-suite.ts` (also fixing a latent miss where `runOpenAIEmptyCompletionTest` was imported but never called). New `runUnconditionalAssistantCoercedToUserTest` in `apps/api/test/control-internal-scheduled-action.service.test.ts` asserts a `audience="assistant"` create with no `actionPayload` is rewritten to `audience="user"` (DB row, telegram reminder target persisted, `coercedFromAudience: "assistant"` in the response). `apps/api/test/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.test.ts` is rewritten to pin the new executor-style prompt shape (with-payload branch and no-payload branch). Verification gate: `pnpm --filter @persai/api lint` / `typecheck` / `test` green; `pnpm --filter @persai/provider-gateway lint` / `typecheck` / `test` green; `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime lint` / `typecheck` / `test` green.

  **Out of scope (deliberate).** No schema bloat — we did not introduce a `kind` or `executionMode` discriminator on the `scheduled_action` tool input schema. The simpler "empty actionPayload → coerce" heuristic is enough to fix the observed live failure mode, and the model-visible tool result's `warning` field gives the model a learning signal without forcing every caller to learn a new schema field. No retroactive cleanup of already-disabled tasks (the founder's test row `fc23766c-…` and any siblings will be cleaned up manually by the founder per the in-session decision). The `Prefer silence` line is preserved in chat-surface system prompts elsewhere — only the assistant-side scheduled-action brief is changed, because that is the surface where silence is a real failure mode.

- **Background scheduled-action stack: fail-soft observability + presence-baseline UUID crash + unified retry/dead-letter contract + anti-duplicate prompt guidance (founder repro on `persai-dev` after T1/T2 closeout — "фоновые задачи не срабатывают и асистент не push и иногда вместо одной делает сразу 2, одну для себя одну для user, и часть, которая за фоновые задачи отвечает, очень сырая — посмотри логи для начала"; this is a single FIX bundle, intentionally not modelled as a new ADR slice):** GKE log dive across `api` / `provider-gateway` / `runtime` pods turned up four interlocking regressions in the proactive-push / scheduled-action stack that all needed to land together for the founder's "фоновые таски и push" path to be trustworthy again. **(1) Provider-gateway exception logging was producing `{"level":50,"context":"ExceptionsHandler","msg":{}}`** for every upstream LLM 500: Nest's default `ExceptionsHandler` invokes `LoggerService.error(error, stack, context)` with the raw `Error` object as `message`, but every `AppLoggerService` in the repo (`apps/api`, `apps/runtime`, `apps/provider-gateway`) typed `message: string` and routed the value through pino's `mergingObject` arg, where Error instances serialise to `{}` because they have no own enumerable properties. We were operationally blind on every provider-gateway exception. **Fix:** new shared helper `normalizeErrorLogPayload(message, trace)` in `@persai/logger` extracts `name` / `message` / `stack` / `cause` (with `cause` itself unwrapped if it's an Error), and the three `AppLoggerService` implementations (`apps/api`, `apps/runtime`, `apps/provider-gateway`) all widen `error()` / `fatal()` to `unknown` and route through the helper. Side effect: every prior call site that already passes a string keeps working byte-for-byte. **(2) `PersaiScheduledActionSchedulerService` was emitting unstructured `Scheduled action <uuid> failed: <message>` strings** that we could not slice by `audience` / `scheduleKind` / `attemptCount` / `decision` in `gcloud logging read`. **Fix:** every failure decision in `processClaimedTask`'s catch branch now emits a structured event (`scheduled_action_failed_deferred`, `scheduled_action_failed_advanced_to_next_recurring_run`, `task_disabled_after_exhausted_retries`) with `{ taskId, externalRef, audience, scheduleKind, attemptCount, decision, errorName, errorMessage, …backoffMs }` so live ops can pivot any of those fields without parsing a sentence. **(3) T1 presence-baseline lookup was crashing on every non-UUID idempotency key,** which in practice means **every** scheduled-action turn — `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-context-hydration.service.ts:computePresenceBlock` was passing `id: { not: input.idempotencyKey }` straight into `prisma.assistantChatMessage.findFirst`, but `AssistantChatMessage.id` is a Postgres `uuid` column and `RuntimeTurnRequest.idempotencyKey` is a free-form string. Scheduled actions inject `"scheduled-action:<externalRef>:<runAtMs>"`, Postgres rejected it with `Inconsistent column data: Error creating UUID, expected …, found 's' at 1`, the existing `try / catch` swallowed the error, and presence rendered with **null timestamps** every time — fully defeating the T1 "sense of time" guarantee on the very codepath (assistant-side proactive runs) that needs it most. **Fix:** new exported predicate `isUuidLikeIdempotencyKey(value)` (strict 8-4-4-4-12 hex regex). The `id: { not: ... }` clause is now applied only when the key matches; non-matching keys (every scheduled-action turn) skip the exclusion entirely. The legitimate web-chat case where `idempotencyKey` is a UUID generated upstream still works exactly as before. **(4) Both audiences had broken retry/lifecycle hygiene.** `audience="assistant"` was disabling silently after 5 receipt-rows by counting `RuntimeTurnReceipt.where(externalThreadKey, status in ("failed","interrupted"))`; that counter saturated within ~1.5 wall-clock minutes because a single failing turn produced multiple receipt rows (one per native tool-loop iteration), so `d7277de7 дёргался 3 раза подряд за минуту и затих` — disabled with **zero** observable signal. `audience="user"` had no cap at all and kept re-firing every flat 30 s forever. **Fix:** new column `attempt_count INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` plus `last_error_message VARCHAR(2000)` and `last_error_at TIMESTAMPTZ(6)` on `assistant_task_registry_items` via reversible additive migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260423040000_adr074_f1_scheduler_attempt_tracking/migration.sql`. The scheduler claim path projects `attemptCount` into the in-memory `ClaimedScheduledAction`. The catch branch now bumps `attemptCount` exactly once per `processClaimedTask` invocation that ends in a failure-and-retry decision, defers with exponential backoff `min(30s · 2^(attempt-1), 1h)` (new exported helper `computeRetryBackoffMs`), and disables the task after `MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5` for **both** audiences with a structured `task_disabled_after_exhausted_retries` log line that includes the truncated last-error message. Recurring `audience="assistant"` tasks (`schedule.kind !== "at"`) preserve their prior "advance to next slot on a non-still-processing failure" behaviour so a failing daily probe does not get permanently disabled — they advance, and `attemptCount` is unaffected by a later success-reset on the next slot. Success in `completeUserActionRun` and `completeAssistantActionRun` resets `attemptCount = 0`, `lastErrorMessage = null`, `lastErrorAt = null`. The unused `countFailedAssistantActionReceipts` helper and the `ASSISTANT_SCHEDULED_ACTION_MAX_FAILED_RECEIPTS` / `SCHEDULED_ACTION_RETRY_DELAY_MS` constants were removed. **(5) Anti-duplicate prompt guidance + soft diagnostic warn** because the founder also repro'd `иногда вместо одной делает сразу 2, одну для себя одну для user`: the model would create both an `audience="assistant"` probe and an `audience="user"` reminder for the same intent in a single turn (e.g. "поставь себе задачу пнуть меня через 2 минуты"). The `scheduled_action.modelUsageGuidance` in `apps/api/prisma/tool-catalog-data.ts` and rule 6 of `buildScheduledActionPrompt` in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/run-scheduled-assistant-action.service.ts` now explicitly forbid creating both audiences for the same intent in the same turn — the correct pattern is "one `audience="user"` for an explicit user-facing nudge", or "one `audience="assistant"` that, when it later fires, conditionally creates one `audience="user"` follow-up with `delayMs=1`". `ControlInternalScheduledActionService.createScheduledAction` additionally emits a soft `duplicate_audience_create_detected` warn with `{ assistantId, newTaskId, newTaskAudience, siblingTaskId, siblingAudience, normalizedTitle }` when the new task's normalized title matches a task with the opposite audience created within the last 60 s by the same assistant — diagnostic only, the row is still created so a legitimate same-title-but-distinct edge case never silently breaks. **Tests.** New focused regressions: `apps/api/test/scheduled-action-retry-backoff.test.ts` pins the exponential curve (30 s / 1 m / 2 m / 4 m / 8 m), the 1-h ceiling at attempt 10 + 99, and the floor-to-1 normalization for absurd inputs. `apps/api/test/normalize-error-log-payload.test.ts` covers Error / Error-with-cause / string + trace / object / circular-object cases. `apps/runtime/test/presence-baseline-uuid-guard.test.ts` pins the predicate's rejection of `scheduled-action:<…>` shapes, almost-UUIDs, null/undefined, and empty strings, plus acceptance of canonical 8-4-4-4-12 (case-insensitive). The existing `apps/api/test/persai-scheduled-action-scheduler.service.test.ts` was migrated off the dead `failedReceiptsByExternalRef` plumbing — `runAssistantFailureExhaustionTest` now seeds `attemptCount: 4` (so the next-attempt bump trips `MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5`) and `runRecurringAssistantFailureDoesNotDisableAtReceiptCapTest` confirms a recurring task at `attemptCount: 4` still **advances** rather than disabling. **Out of scope (deliberate).** No new ADR slice — the founder's call was "это по части FIX а не архитектура серьёзная, запиши только в историю правок"; the entire bundle lives in CHANGELOG + SESSION-HANDOFF only. The admin task-list "failed" pill that uses the new `lastErrorMessage` is intentionally deferred — the column is populated and visible in admin DB inspection now, but the UI surfacing is left for a follow-up so this fix stays observability-/lifecycle-focused.
