The `provider-gateway` HTTP exception filter itself was not changed (the issue was always upstream of it, in the logger service); request-context fields like `requestId` flow through Nest's existing `request-id` middleware unchanged. Verification gate: `pnpm --filter @persai/api typecheck` / `lint` / `tsx test/{persai-scheduled-action-scheduler.service,scheduled-action-retry-backoff,normalize-error-log-payload,control-internal-scheduled-action.service}.test.ts` all green; `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime typecheck` / `lint` / `tsx test/presence-baseline-uuid-guard.test.ts` green; `pnpm --filter @persai/provider-gateway typecheck` / `lint` green; `pnpm format:check` clean.

- **Web chat slow-mo cadence watchdog no longer false-fires on long tool calls — silent timer is now suspended for the full tool-execution span (founder repro on `persai-dev` while asking for two `image_generate` results; confirmed by GKE logs):** the founder reported the red `Streaming ended before a full answer was completed.` banner under the chat composer when asking for image generation. GKE `api` pod logs confirmed the false-positive shape: `web_stream_stall_detected reason=silent silentMs=8000 rollingAvgMs=n/a rollingWindow=n/a observedGaps=0 accumulatedLen=0` ~11 s after `web_runtime_route` for an `image_generate`-driven turn, i.e. the silent watchdog fired with **zero** observed text-delta gaps and an empty accumulated text — the model had only emitted a tool call so far. **Root cause.** `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/cadence-watchdog.ts` exposes two stall reasons: `slow_avg` (correctly text-only — fed only by `recordDelta()`) and `silent` (an 8 s "no activity" timer reset by any `recordActivity()` call). The web-chat consumer in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts` was calling `watchdog.recordActivity()` on `chunk.type === "tool"` for both `toolPhase === "start"` and `toolPhase === "end"`. That correctly reset the silent timer at `tool_started`, but the timer then ticked through the tool's actual execution span (`image_generate` / `video_generate` / slow `web_fetch` routinely take 15–60 s with no intermediate chunks), so at ~`silentMs` the watchdog fired, `internalAbort.abort()` killed the runtime fetch (`stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts:723`), `streamRuntimeAttempt` returned `status: "stalled"`, the `safeToRetry` check failed (`toolEventCount > 0` because `tool_started` had already passed) so no retry was attempted, `accumulated === ""` and `collectedMedia === []` (the image was not yet delivered — we aborted before `tool_finished`), and the API returned `{ status: "failed", code: "runtime_invalid_response", message: "Runtime stream finished without assistant output." }`. The web client classifier in `apps/web/app/app/assistant-api-client.ts:666` matches any error message containing the substring `"stream"` and surfaces the bilingual `"Streaming ended before a full answer was completed."` banner — exactly the founder's screenshot. **Fix.** The watchdog now exposes two new methods, `recordToolStarted()` / `recordToolFinished()`, that maintain an `inflightToolCount` and **suspend** the silent timer for the union of all in-flight tool spans — `startSilentTimer()` short-circuits when the counter is `> 0`, and `recordToolFinished()` re-arms the timer with `lastDeltaAtMs = now()` once the last tool resolves. Both methods also move the inter-delta anchor forward (mirroring the existing `recordActivity` semantics) so resumed text deltas after the tool finishes are not penalized by the tool's execution span polluting the `slow_avg` rolling window. `recordToolFinished()` tolerates over-decrement defensively (extra calls are no-ops, the counter never goes negative) so a duplicate end event from upstream demuxing cannot indefinitely keep the suspension active. The web-chat consumer (`stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts`) now calls `watchdog.recordToolStarted()` on `chunk.toolPhase === "start"` and `watchdog.recordToolFinished()` on `chunk.toolPhase === "end"` instead of the generic `recordActivity()`, so the silent watchdog now strictly guards **text** cadence (its original design intent — per-tool execution timeouts live in the provider gateway / runtime, not the cadence watchdog). The `slow_avg` branch is unchanged: it was always text-only and remains so. `chunk.type === "thinking" / "media" / "done"` continue to use `recordActivity()` because those are genuine progress signals during the text phase. **Tests.** Five new unit tests in `apps/api/test/cadence-watchdog.test.ts` (the suite grows from 14 to 19 tests, all green): (1) `recordToolStarted` suspends the silent timer for the entire tool span (60 s tool with `silentMs = 5000` does not fire, then `recordToolFinished` re-arms and fires `silentMs` later), (2) `recordToolStarted` clears an already-armed silent timer (healthy text streaming → tool starts mid-stream → timer is suspended even if it was previously armed by `recordDelta`), (3) overlapping tools (counter 0→1→2 then 2→1→0) keep the timer suspended until the **last** finish, (4) over-decrement is tolerated (extra `recordToolFinished` calls do not push the counter negative or break a subsequent genuine tool span), (5) tool spans do not pollute `slow_avg` of resumed text deltas (45 s tool span between two healthy text bursts does not flag `slow_avg`). **Out of scope.** This fix only touches the web-chat consumer (`stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts`); the Telegram consumer (`send-native-telegram-turn.service.ts`) does not use the cadence watchdog, so there is no parallel change there. The watchdog API change is additive (existing `recordActivity` semantics unchanged), so nothing else in the codebase needs to migrate. The classifier mapping in `apps/web/app/app/assistant-api-client.ts` that catches any `"stream"` substring is intentionally left as-is — it is the correct catch-all for genuine stream-incomplete cases; the fix removes the **false** trigger source instead of papering over it on the client. Verification gate: `pnpm --filter @persai/api typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/api lint` clean, `pnpm exec prettier --check` clean on the three touched files, `pnpm --filter @persai/api test` clean (full suite green), `pnpm --filter @persai/api exec node --import tsx --test test/cadence-watchdog.test.ts` reports `# tests 19 # pass 19 # fail 0` (5 new + 14 existing).

- **ADR-074 Memory Center "Session expired" — actual root cause fix (the previous two attempts were both wrong; this one was found by reading GKE logs side-by-side instead of guessing):** the founder reported the inline `Session expired. Sign in again and refresh the page.` banner kept appearing on the Memory Center even after `c5ee67cd` (which forced `getToken({ skipCache: true })` on every read path and added a verifyToken-failure-reason WARN log on the API). The new WARN log was the smoking gun: zero entries in `gcloud logging read … resource.labels.container_name=api AND jsonPayload.context=ClerkAuthService`, but the `request_completed` audit lane on the same pod showed 401 responses on `POST /api/v1/assistant/memory/items/<id>/close-open-loop` with `userId=null` and `latencyMs ≈ 1.28` — i.e. the request finished in ~1ms, far less than any Clerk verifyToken roundtrip, and ClerkAuthService.resolveAuthenticatedUser was never even reached. Same browser, same JWT, the GETs `/api/v1/assistant/memory/items` and `/api/v1/assistant/memory/workspace/items` immediately before and after returned `200` for the same `userId`, proving the token was perfectly valid. Real cause: `apps/api/src/modules/identity-access/identity-access.module.ts` lists the routes that `ClerkAuthMiddleware` is mounted on as an explicit allow-list of `{ path, method }` pairs, and **the close-open-loop route was never added to that list when M3.1 introduced it**. Without the middleware, `req.resolvedAppUser` was `undefined` when the request hit `AssistantController.closeOpenLoopMemoryItem`, so the controller's `resolveRequestUserId` immediately threw `UnauthorizedException("Authenticated user context is missing.")` — a real 401 from the handler, not from token verification. The api-client's `toErrorMessage` mapped any `ContractsApiError.status === 401` to the literal string `"Session expired. Sign in again and refresh the page."`, which the new M3.3 inline `FeedbackLine` rendered under the Memory section. So the founder kept seeing "Session expired" on a perfectly valid session because the route was effectively un-authenticated and was self-rejecting in the controller body. Fix: one new entry `{ path: "api/v1/assistant/memory/items/:itemId/close-open-loop", method: RequestMethod.POST }` in the `ClerkAuthMiddleware.forRoutes(...)` block in `apps/api/src/modules/identity-access/identity-access.module.ts`. Locked with a regression assertion in `apps/api/test/identity-access.module.test.ts` (`hasRoute(...)` for the close-open-loop POST, with a failure message that explains why this route specifically must be guarded — to prevent the same drop-off the next time an endpoint is added to `AssistantController`). Also reverted the misguided `getToken({ skipCache: true })` calls on the load paths (`loadAll` / `reloadChats` in `apps/web/app/app/_components/use-app-data.ts`; voice-settings load + `loadMemory` / `loadTasks` / `loadWsMemory` in `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.tsx`) that the previous attempt had added — they were defending against a different failure mode (token actually expired) which the GKE logs proved is not happening here, and `skipCache:true` on every page load would needlessly hammer Clerk's refresh endpoint on every `data.reload()` cycle. The earlier hotfix's `skipCache:true` on **mutations** in `assistant-settings.tsx` and the `Reload` button on `FeedbackLine` are kept (they remain a cheap last-resort recovery for any genuinely-expired token in the future). The diagnostic WARN logging in `apps/api/src/modules/identity-access/infrastructure/identity/clerk-auth.service.ts` and the seven `classifyClerkVerifyFailure` unit tests in `apps/api/test/clerk-auth.service.test.ts` from `c5ee67cd` are kept as well — they did not cause the bug, they were what finally proved the previous theory wrong by staying silent during the live repro.
- **ADR-074 Memory Center "Session expired" follow-up — root-cause fix for the inline `Session expired. Sign in again and refresh the page.` cycle (the founder's previous report that the prior `a782d36d` `skipCache:true` + `Reload` button hotfix only papered over the symptom):** the prior hotfix added `getToken({ skipCache: true })` on every **mutation** handler in `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.tsx` (`handleSaveAndApply`, `handleRollback`, `handleReset`, `handleForget`, `handleCloseOpenLoop`, `handleAddWsMemory`, `handleForgetWsMemory`, `handleTaskAction`, `handleNotificationPreferenceChange`, avatar upload) plus a one-click `Reload` recovery button on `FeedbackLine` when the inline error text matches `Session expired`. After deploy, GKE logs (`gcloud logging read … resource.labels.container_name=api AND jsonPayload.status=401`, freshness 24h) showed every 401 was coming from `POST /api/v1/assistant/memory/items/<id>/close-open-loop` with `userId=null` (i.e. `ClerkAuthMiddleware` rejected the bearer before the route handler — see `apps/api/src/modules/identity-access/infrastructure/identity/clerk-auth.service.ts`'s `verifyToken(...).catch(() => throw new UnauthorizedException("Invalid Clerk token."))`); all 401s landed on the **pre-hotfix** ReplicaSets (`api-7888ccfcdc-*`, `api-75964b5b87-*`), so the founder's screenshot was captured before image `7a442e36` was rolled out — but the underlying root-cause was still alive in the codebase, because the hotfix only covered mutations and **not the load-functions that the post-mutation `data.reload()` re-invokes via `useEffect`**: `loadMemory` (line 803), `loadTasks` (line 821), `loadWsMemory` (line 839), the voice-settings load (line 705), plus `useAppData.loadAll` (`apps/web/app/app/_components/use-app-data.ts:64`) and `useAppData.reloadChats` (`:106`). All six were calling `getToken()` (cached). The reproducible loop was: founder clicks any mutation → `skipCache:true` mutation succeeds → the success handler calls `data.reload()` → `useAppData.loadAll` reuses the same cached token that has now crossed Clerk's accepted lifetime → `getAssistant(...)` etc. throw a `ContractsApiError(status=401)` → `toErrorMessage` returns the literal `"Session expired. Sign in again and refresh the page."` → the `useAppData` `error` state propagates back into the consuming component → `FeedbackLine` renders the bilingual banner the founder reported, immediately after a click that actually succeeded. **Frontend fix:** every load-function on the `/app` route now also force-refreshes the Clerk JWT — symmetric to the mutation handlers — by switching to `getToken({ skipCache: true })`. Edited: `assistant-settings.tsx` (`loadMemory`, `loadTasks`, `loadWsMemory`, the voice-settings effect at line 705) and `use-app-data.ts` (`loadAll`, `reloadChats`). The `Reload` button stays as a fallback for genuinely-dead sessions where even a fresh fetch returns 401 — it is now correctly the last-resort surface, not the first one. **Backend diagnostic fix (one of the two reasons the founder pushed back on the previous hotfix — "you cannot tell what is actually breaking, you just papered over the UX"):** `clerk-auth.service.ts`'s `resolveAuthenticatedUser` previously swallowed every `verifyToken` failure into a single opaque `UnauthorizedException("Invalid Clerk token.")` with no log; an attached `pino` `request_completed` line at level `30` was the only signal in GKE logs, and it carried `userId: null` and `status: 401` with no clue whether the token was expired, badly-signed, audience-mismatched, malformed, or the Clerk JWKS endpoint flaked. The new `classifyClerkVerifyFailure(error: unknown): ClerkVerifyFailureReason` (exported for unit tests) maps the upstream `error.reason | error.code | error.message` substring into a bounded enum (`token_expired | token_not_active_yet | invalid_signature | invalid_audience | invalid_issuer | malformed_token | jwks_fetch_failed | unknown`); the `verifyToken(...).catch(...)` block now emits `WARN [ClerkAuthService] Clerk verifyToken failed: reason=<one_of_those_eight> upstream="<original message>"` before throwing `UnauthorizedException("Invalid Clerk token (<reason>).")`. The `clerkClient.users.getUser(...)` follow-up failure now also logs `WARN [ClerkAuthService] Clerk users.getUser(<sub>) failed: <upstream message>`; a missing `sub` claim in the verified payload now logs a one-line `WARN [ClerkAuthService] Clerk verifyToken succeeded but payload is missing 'sub' claim.`. None of the log lines contain the bearer token itself; cardinality is bounded by the eight-value enum so `gcloud logging read` queries stay cheap. **Tests.** `apps/api/test/clerk-auth.service.test.ts` (NEW, 7 unit tests) locks the classifier on each branch — expired (three input shapes), nbf, signature, audience/issuer, malformed/decode, jwks/network, and the `unknown` fallback for unrecognized errors / `null` / numbers / empty objects. The classifier is a pure function, so the test fake-injects upstream `Error` instances directly without touching Clerk SDK. Verification gate: `pnpm format:check` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/api lint` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/web lint` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/api typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/web typecheck` clean, the new classifier test suite passes 7/7 under `pnpm --filter ./apps/api exec tsx --test test/clerk-auth.service.test.ts`. **Acceptance.** Post-deploy, the next time the founder triggers a Memory Center action that would have previously surfaced `Session expired`, GKE logs will now record the **actual** Clerk verification reason (expected `token_expired` for the original report, but the WARN line will tell us if it is something else like `jwks_fetch_failed` from a Clerk-side flake or `invalid_signature` from a misconfigured environment). The frontend should no longer surface the inline banner at all on a normal mutation → reload cycle, because every read is now equally fresh-token. If the inline banner does surface again after this fix, the WARN log gives us exactly one substring to grep on (`reason=`) to make the next fix root-cause-first.

### Added

- **ADR-074 Slice T2 — Auto-route T1 pushes to first-bound notification channel (code-landed in code; verification gate green, awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live UI gates):** the preferred-channel notification path used by `HandleInternalCronFireService.execute` for every `audience="user"` scheduled action — i.e. every T1 proactive push — was already capable of routing notifications through Telegram, but the live behaviour was always "land in web chat" because `Assistant.preferredNotificationChannel` defaulted to `"web"` and was never auto-flipped on bind. T2 closes that one missing bit: a fresh non-web-channel bind now promotes `preferredNotificationChannel` to that channel — once — while honouring any explicit prior choice the user has made through Settings. **Schema.** Single additive nullable column `preferredNotificationChannelChosenAt TIMESTAMPTZ(6) NULL` on `Assistant` via reversible migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260423010000_adr074_t2_preferred_notification_channel_chosen_at/migration.sql`. The column is the "D-marker" from the founder interview (Q2-D): NULL means "still on the `web` default — never explicitly chosen", non-NULL means "user has actively picked a channel; do not auto-override". No new index — the column is read together with the assistant row by primary key. **One-time SQL backfill (Q7-B), in the same migration file.** `UPDATE assistants` promotes any assistant where `preferred_notification_channel_chosen_at IS NULL AND preferred_notification_channel = 'web' AND EXISTS (... assistant_channel_surface_bindings ... provider_key='telegram' ... binding_state='active' ... metadata->>'telegramDmChatId' IS NOT NULL)` to `preferred_notification_channel='telegram'` and stamps `chosen_at = NOW()`. Idempotent by construction: re-running the migration is a no-op because every row touched the first time now has a non-null timestamp. The `metadata->>'telegramDmChatId' IS NOT NULL` guard ensures we never auto-flip a binding that is mid-claim and lacks the DM-target metadata that Telegram delivery actually needs. The founder's existing TG-bound `persai-dev` assistant is the primary beneficiary: post-deploy, the very next T1 push routes through the existing TG path with no UI action required. **New helper service `AutoSelectNotificationChannelOnBindService`** (`apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/auto-select-notification-channel-on-bind.service.ts`, ~95 lines including doc-comments) implements the conditional compare-and-set: given `{ assistantId, bindingChannel }` (where `bindingChannel ∈ {"telegram","whatsapp"}` — `web` is rejected as non-promotable), it does a single `assistant.findUnique` + a single conditional `assistant.updateMany` whose `where` clause replicates the `preferredNotificationChannelChosenAt: null` predicate. The `updateMany.count === 0` branch covers the (vanishingly narrow) race where two bind hooks fire concurrently or a manual preference update lands between the read and the write — the helper surfaces it as `{ changed: false, reason: "already_chosen" }` rather than a phantom `auto_set`. Return shape `{ changed: boolean, reason: "auto_set" | "already_chosen" | "channel_already_matches" | "assistant_not_found" }` is for observability — callers ignore it today, but it is structured so a future `/admin` panel could surface "auto-promoted" events. **Bind-completion hook in `SyncTelegramChatTargetService`** (`apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/sync-telegram-chat-target.service.ts`): the existing `claimOwner && isPrivateChat` branch (the existing path that writes `telegramOwnerClaimStatus = "claimed"` and `telegramDmChatId` into binding metadata) now also calls `autoSelectNotificationChannelOnBindService.execute({ assistantId, bindingChannel: "telegram" })` AFTER `patchMetadata` succeeds — ordering matters because any subsequent Telegram delivery lookup must see the new `telegramDmChatId`. The call is wrapped in `try/catch` so a helper failure logs `WARN [SyncTelegramChatTargetService] AutoSelectNotificationChannelOnBind failed for assistant ... after Telegram owner-claim; bind succeeded but preferred channel left unchanged: ...` and the bind itself still succeeds (best-effort, hard constraint: TG claim must not regress). Group-chat updates and non-claim metadata refreshes deliberately do NOT trigger the auto-select — they are not bind completions. **D-marker write in manual updates.** `UpdateAssistantNotificationPreferenceService` (`apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/update-assistant-notification-preference.service.ts`) now writes `preferredNotificationChannelChosenAt: new Date()` on every successful manual preference update through the Settings UI, including downgrades back to `web`. This is what protects the founder's explicit choice ("I clicked `web` after binding TG") against the auto-select helper firing on a subsequent re-claim — once non-NULL, the helper short-circuits as `already_chosen` regardless of channel. **Wiring.** `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/workspace-management.module.ts` registers `AutoSelectNotificationChannelOnBindService` as a provider; `SyncTelegramChatTargetService` injects it via constructor (NestJS standard DI, no `@Inject` token needed because it is a class-based provider). **Note on DI footgun.** Per the M2/T1 precedent, the helper class is imported as a value (`import { AutoSelectNotificationChannelOnBindService }`), NOT as `import type`, because Nest needs the class symbol at runtime to resolve the dependency — `import type` for an injectable is the known footgun that produces `UnknownDependenciesException` at boot. **Tests.** Three new test files. `apps/api/test/auto-select-notification-channel-on-bind.service.test.ts` (6 unit tests with a duck-typed Prisma fake): `chosenAt NULL` promotes channel + writes timestamp, `chosenAt` already set is a no-op, channel-already-matches writes the marker only (so the next call short-circuits), assistant-not-found is best-effort no-op, concurrent update race (forced `updateMany.count === 0`) falls back to `already_chosen`, non-promotable channel `web` is rejected without any DB read. `apps/api/test/sync-telegram-chat-target.service.test.ts` (5 integration tests with fake binding repo + fake helper): owner-claim + private chat triggers exactly one helper call with the right arguments, non-claim metadata refresh (e.g. runtime-health update) does NOT trigger auto-select, group-chat claim does NOT trigger auto-select, helper failure does not break the bind, and an explicit ordering test asserts `patchMetadata` runs before `autoSelect`. `apps/api/test/update-assistant-notification-preference.service.test.ts` (4 tests with fake Prisma + fake audit service): manual update writes `chosenAt` inside the call window, downgrading back to `web` still writes a fresh `chosenAt`, rejected updates (channel not in `availableChannels`) do not write `chosenAt`, missing assistant throws `NotFoundException`. Existing T1 + scheduler + audit + reminder-delivery suites continue to pass without modification. Verification gate this session: `pnpm --filter ./apps/api prisma:generate` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/api typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter ./apps/api lint` clean, `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean across all 14 workspace projects, `pnpm --filter ./apps/api test` clean (full suite incl. the three new test files), `pnpm --filter @persai/web typecheck` clean, `pnpm format:check` clean (the three new test files were prettier-written before the recheck). The four founder live UI gates run **after** image publish + Argo CD rollout (the api-migrate job runs the backfill SQL during rollout): (1) refresh `persai-dev` Settings → "Reminder delivery" pill must show `Telegram` selected for the founder assistant (backfill effect — no UI action required), (2) create a one-shot scheduled action with `delayMs ≈ 60s` and `audience="user"` for the founder assistant → push must arrive in the TG bot DM (not in web chat), (3) flip the Settings pill back to `Web` → create another one-shot push → push must arrive in web chat (manual override invariant), (4) spin up a fresh staging assistant with no TG bound → bind TG via the bot → confirm Settings now shows `Telegram` selected automatically and a new push lands in TG. **Code-archaeology note.** The original Slice T2 spec in ADR-074 (committed before this session) proposed building a `ChannelDeliveryRouter` + `SendNativeTelegramOutboundService` + modifying `RunScheduledAssistantActionService` and runtime `channel: "telegram"` handling. Reading the actual scheduler/delivery code revealed that `RunScheduledAssistantActionService` is only invoked for `audience="assistant"` (background fact-check turns that land in web chat); `audience="user"` T1 pushes go through the direct preferred-channel notification path from `HandleInternalCronFireService`. The existing TG outbound infrastructure was therefore complete — only `preferredNotificationChannel` being stuck on `"web"` blocked the live path. The ADR-074 Slice T2 section was rewritten in the same commit (under "Slice T2 — Auto-route T1 pushes to first-bound notification channel") to reflect the real scope: 7 design questions distilled from a structured interview (Q1-B full reroute via auto-select, Q2-D respect explicit prior choice, Q3-A only `preferredNotificationChannel`, Q4-A trigger inside `SyncTelegramChatTargetService`, Q5-B generalize to a helper, Q6-C unit + integration + manual founder gates without live E2E TG bot, Q7-B one-time SQL backfill), no new `proactive-push-tg.yaml` smoke scenario, no router, no runtime channel changes. T1 safeguards (`ProactivePushPolicyService`, 1/48h, quiet hours, auto-mute) continue to fire because they gate inside the scheduler BEFORE `HandleInternalCronFireService` is even called — channel switch does not bypass the policy gate.
- **ADR-074 Slice T1 — sense of time + frequency safeguards (code-landed in code; verification gate green, awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live UI gates):** combined T1 slice ships two products together (founder hard constraint #1 — both ship in one commit). **(A) Sense of time (presence).** A NEW `presence` prompt template (parallel sibling of `heartbeat`, NOT an extension of it — hard constraint #2) renders four always-present per-turn fields into the developer-tail: `time_since_last_user_message_in_thread`, `time_since_last_user_message_anywhere` (reuses M3.2 cross-thread `lastUserMessageAt` data path; no new repository method per #6), `current_local_time` (`HH:MM` user TZ), `current_local_weekday` (e.g. `Monday` / `понедельник`). The block carries a usage-rule paragraph telling the model NOT to recite timestamps back to the user — "behave like a friend who quietly notices the time, not like a clock that reports it." Presence text lives entirely in `developerInstructions`; changing the presence template MUST NOT change `systemPrompt` / `stablePrefix.hash` (P1 invariant — hard constraint #3, locked by `runPresenceCachedPrefixInvariant` in `apps/api/test/compile-prompt-constructor.service.test.ts`). Developer-tail order is fixed at `routingGuidance → presence → heartbeat`. The bilingual time-ago formatter required by hard constraint #5 was extracted into a new shared module `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/relative-time-formatter.ts` (English + Russian with proper Russian pluralization rules) and re-exported from `cross-session-carry-over-renderer.ts`; M3 keeps using the helper without a locale arg (English-only, byte-for-byte preserved), the new presence renderer in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/presence-renderer.ts` passes `userContext.locale` explicitly. Resolves an ADR-vs-code reconciliation surfaced this session: the ADR claimed M3's formatter was already bilingual, but inspection showed it was English-only — the extraction satisfies BOTH the reuse and the bilingual requirement without parallel formatters. **(B) Frequency safeguards (proactive-push policy).** New `ProactivePushPolicyService` (`apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/proactive-push-policy.service.ts`) enforces three rules on `audience="user"` scheduled actions: max 1 push per 48h (defer to `lastFiredAt + 48h`), 22:00–09:00 local quiet hours (defer to next 09:00 local using `Intl.DateTimeFormat` with a 2-pass timezone-offset solver to handle DST correctly), and 14-day auto-mute after 2 consecutive unanswered pushes (released on ANY user-initiated message — broader than "answered the specific push" per hard constraint #10). The five policy constants live in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/proactive-push-policy.constants.ts` (`MIN_INTERVAL_HOURS = 48`, `QUIET_HOURS_START_LOCAL = 22`, `QUIET_HOURS_END_LOCAL = 9`, `AUTO_MUTE_AFTER_UNANSWERED = 2`, `AUTO_MUTE_DURATION_DAYS = 14`, `ANSWERED_WINDOW_HOURS = 24`); NO admin surface, NO plan-policy fields, NO per-workspace overrides — Principle 1 (hard constraint #8). The gate fires only on `audience="user"` (hard constraint #11; locked by an explicit `runAssistantAudienceSkipsPolicyGateTest` that asserts the policy mock is NOT invoked on the assistant-side path). `lastFiredAt` is bumped atomically with the existing claim release in `PersaiScheduledActionSchedulerService`, only after the user-visible dispatch succeeds (hard constraint #12; locked by `runUserAudienceAllowedBumpsLastFiredAtAtomicallyTest` and `runUserAudienceFailedDispatchSkipsLastFiredBumpTest`). **Schema.** Three additive columns on `AssistantTaskRegistryItem` — `lastFiredAt`, `lastAnsweredCheckAt`, `consecutiveUnanswered Int @default(0)` — via single reversible additive migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260423000000_adr074_t1_proactive_push_safeguards/migration.sql`. NO new `proactive_push_log` table, NO new index — the scheduler already filters on the existing partial-index, and the per-claim policy lookup is O(1) by primary key (hard constraint #7). **Tests.** 13 new policy unit tests covering every branch (assistant-allow, first-ever push, interval defer, quiet-hours defer in three sub-cases, auto-mute defer, auto-mute release on user message, unanswered-counter idempotent bump, all-clear allow, constants ship-values, bad-tz UTC fallback, interval beats quiet hours); 4 new scheduler-integration tests covering the new policy gate; 1 new compile-prompt-constructor invariant test for the P1 invariant on `presence`; 2 new runtime test files (`relative-time-formatter.test.ts` for the bilingual formatter, `presence-renderer.test.ts` for the per-turn block render). Files touched: `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/relative-time-formatter.ts` (NEW), `cross-session-carry-over-renderer.ts`, `presence-renderer.ts` (NEW), `turn-context-hydration.service.ts`, `turn-execution.service.ts`; `packages/runtime-bundle/src/index.ts`; `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/{compile-prompt-constructor.service.ts,materialize-assistant-published-version.service.ts,proactive-push-policy.constants.ts,proactive-push-policy.service.ts,persai-scheduled-action-scheduler.service.ts}`; `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/workspace-management.module.ts`; `apps/api/prisma/{schema.prisma,bootstrap-preset-data.ts}` + new migration; `apps/web/app/admin/presets/page.tsx`. Verification gate this session: `pnpm --filter @persai/api prisma:generate` clean, `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean (0 warnings on touched files), `pnpm run format:check` clean (4 newly-touched files were prettier-written before the check), `pnpm --filter @persai/api run typecheck` / `@persai/web run typecheck` / `@persai/runtime run typecheck` / `@persai/runtime-contract run typecheck` all clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/api test` clean (full suite incl. new policy + scheduler-integration + compile-constructor invariant tests), `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test` clean (full suite incl. new presence + formatter test files). No new smoke scenario (M3.2 precedent — hard constraint #13). The four founder live UI gates run **after** image publish + Argo CD rollout: (1) developer-tail contains `# Sense of Time` block with the four interpolated values (bilingual when locale is `ru`), (2) model does NOT recite the time-ago / local-time numbers back to the user, (3) `audience="user"` reminder scheduled for 23:30 local is deferred to the next 09:00 local, (4) interval + auto-mute + release-on-user-message lifecycle behaves as specified.
- **ADR-074 Slice M3.3 — live verification on `persai-dev` (4/4 founder live gates green) + real upstream HTTP class for the close-button bug captured = `401 Session expired`:** after M3.3 commit `1d5c7ba` was published + Argo CD-rolled to `persai-dev`, the founder ran the four live gates from the M3.3 entry below. All four passed. Gate 2 (close-button on `open_loop` row removes it OR shows a real error) passed in the "shows a real error" branch — the captured upstream HTTP class is **`401 Session expired`** (the Clerk session JWT had expired between page-load and click; the api-client's `toErrorMessage` mapping for `ContractsApiError.status === 401` returns `"Session expired. Sign in again and refresh the page."`; the new M3.3 inline `FeedbackLine` surfaced it under the Memory section as designed). This is the previously-deferred root cause from the M3.3 commit message and from the M3.3 ADR section — now captured. The pre-M3.3 silent-catch in `handleCloseOpenLoop` was eating exactly this 401 — confirming the silent-catch hypothesis as the click-no-op root cause. No M3.3.1 per-status diagnostic message is required: 401 is a session-wide condition (not Memory-Center-specific) and the existing `Session expired` wording is already actionable. **ADR-074 Slice M3.3 status flips to `Code-landed + deployed + live-verified`** — same flip applied in the ADR M3.3 status block in this commit.
- **`/admin/presets` editor save-spinner hotfix (`PromptTemplateEditor` + `ToolPromptEditor`, same family of silent-failure bug as the pre-M3.3 Memory Center silent-catch — but in editor components instead of handlers):** the **Task Heartbeat** and **Native Tool Runtime** editors on `/admin/presets` previously hung the save spinner forever and never persisted edits when the underlying PATCH threw (the founder hit this on `persai-dev` while trying to delete a word from the heartbeat template that was bleeding into the system prompt). Root cause: both `handleSave` callbacks were structured as `setSaving(true); await onSave(...); setSaving(false); ...` with no try/finally — when `onSave` threw (the `handleSaveTemplate` / `handleSaveTool` callbacks both `throw new Error("Save failed: <status>")` on non-2xx, including 401 `Session expired` from a stale Clerk JWT), the exception propagated up into the `void handleSave()` callsite and `setSaving(false)` was never reached, the `Loader2` spinner spun forever, and the founder could not tell the request had failed. `PersonaArchetypeEditor.handleSave` was already structured correctly with `try { … } catch { setParseError(…) } finally { setSaving(false) }` and an inline `parseError` line; that one stays as the canonical pattern. Hotfix: both `PromptTemplateEditor.handleSave` and `ToolPromptEditor.handleSave` in `apps/web/app/admin/presets/page.tsx` now match the `PersonaArchetypeEditor.handleSave` shape — `setSaveError(null) + setSaving(true) + try { await onSave(...); setSaved(true); ... } catch (cause) { console.error("[admin-presets] <handler> failed", cause); setSaveError(cause.message); } finally { setSaving(false); }`. A new `saveError` state on each editor renders an inline `<p role="alert" className="mt-2 text-[11px] text-red-400">{saveError}</p>` line under the editor body. `PromptTemplateEditor.handleReset` got the same try/catch/finally treatment (it was already wrapped in `try { ... } finally { setResetting(false) }`, but it now also surfaces the error inline instead of silently swallowing it into an unhandled promise rejection). Console errors are tagged `[admin-presets]` to mirror the `[memory-center]` tag from M3.3 for one-line traceability in the dev console. No backend change, no contract change, no Prisma migration. Verification gate: `pnpm -w typecheck` / `pnpm -w lint` / `pnpm -w test` / `pnpm -w build` / `pnpm run format:check` all clean. Live verification deferred to founder eyes-on after deploy: edit the Task Heartbeat template, click Save → either persists with the green checkmark + spinner clears, or the spinner clears and an inline error line surfaces explaining why; same behaviour for the Native Tool Runtime tool editor.
- **ADR-074 Slice M3.3 — Memory Center polish + M3.1 close-button hotfix (code-landed in code; verification gate green, awaiting `persai-dev` deploy + 4 founder live gates):** combined follow-through to M3.1 / M3.2. **(A) Hotfix — Memory Center "Mark as closed" button no longer silently no-ops.** Pre-M3.3, the `handleCloseOpenLoop` handler in `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.tsx` wrapped the `postAssistantMemoryItemCloseOpenLoop` call in `try { … } catch { /* non-critical */ }`. Because the catch was empty, any thrown `Error` from the api-client (the client correctly throws on every non-2xx via the shared `parseJsonOrThrow` path inherited from M2) silently erased: the optimistic `setMemoryItems(prev => prev.filter(...))` in the `try` body was skipped, the spinner cleared via the `finally` block, the user saw "click animates, the open-loop row stays in place, no error" — exactly the symptom the founder hit on `persai-dev` after the M3.1 deploy. M3.3 strips that silent-catch (and the seven other `catch { /* non-critical */ }` blocks across the Memory Center handlers — `loadMemory`, `loadTasks`, `loadWsMemory`, `handleAddWsMemory`, `handleForgetWsMemory`, `handleForget`, `handleTaskAction`) and replaces each with `(a)` an inline bilingual error string surfaced through a section-local `ActionFeedback` slot patterned after the existing `notificationFb` (three new states `memoryFb`, `wsMemoryFb`, `tasksFb` rendered through the existing `FeedbackLine` component above each section's list), plus `(b)` `console.error("[memory-center] <handler> failed", error)` so future debugging in the dev console is one-line traceable. Nine new bilingual i18n keys land in `apps/web/messages/{en,ru}.json` (`memoryResolved`, `memoryLoadFailed`, `memoryForgetFailed`, `memoryCloseOpenLoopFailed`, `wsMemoryLoadFailed`, `wsMemoryAddFailed`, `wsMemoryForgetFailed`, `tasksLoadFailed`, `tasksActionFailed`). The exact upstream HTTP status of the failing close call was NOT directly captured in this session — the founder did not surface a live `kubectl logs` snippet of a failing call and the silent-catch erased the only client-side evidence; the hotfix is therefore status-agnostic-by-design (surface ANY thrown error inline + `console.error` + retain the row, regardless of which HTTP code came back), and the new inline-error UX will surface the real upstream code (400 / 404 / 409 / 500) on the next live click on `persai-dev` so M3.3.1 can refine the per-status diagnostic message if the live click reveals a recurring distinguishable upstream class — otherwise the single bilingual `memoryCloseOpenLoopFailed` string ("We could not mark this item as closed. Please try again." / "Не удалось закрыть открытый вопрос. Попробуйте ещё раз.") is the production shape. **Companion latent-badge fix (same render path):** the pre-M3.3 fallback `kind !== null ? t("memoryKindOpenLoop") : null` mislabelled `fact` and `preference` rows as "ОТКРЫТЫЙ ВОПРОС" in the "История" tab even though the close-button gate (`item.kind === "open_loop"`) was already strict, so clicking the badge area on a `fact` row would show a button-less row labelled "OPEN LOOP" which compounded the confusion; M3.3 replaces it with strict `kind === "open_loop" / "fact" / "preference"` checks plus distinct labels for `fact` (`memoryKindFact`) and `preference` (`memoryKindPreference`) and a new `memoryResolved` "Закрыто" / "Closed" badge for `kind === "open_loop"` rows where `resolvedAt !== null`. The `CheckCircle2` close-button visibility is now gated on `row.source === "registry" && row.item.kind === "open_loop" && row.item.resolvedAt === null` so it is invisible on `fact` / `preference` rows AND on already-resolved open-loop rows. **(B) Memory Center tab merge (UX, UI-side, no backend migration).** "Рабочая область" tab now unifies all curated structured memory (workspace items + structured registry items where `kind ∈ {fact, preference, open_loop}`); "История" tab shows pure conversational echoes only (registry items with `kind = null`, no close-buttons). New pure helper `mergeMemoryViews(registry, workspace): { workspace: MergedMemoryRow[]; history: MergedMemoryRow[] }` in `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.tsx` splits registry items by `kind` into the two tab buckets via the new `STRUCTURED_REGISTRY_KINDS = new Set<["fact","preference","open_loop"]>` and dedupes workspace echoes against the workspace bucket via the new `normalizeMemoryText(text: string): string` helper (lowercase + trim outer whitespace + collapse internal whitespace runs to a single space + strip a single trailing dot). Collision rule: registry-row wins (it owns `kind` / `resolvedAt` / close-button state); the workspace-row is suppressed in the merged view when its normalised text matches a registry row. Two registry rows with the same normalised text are NOT collapsed (they have distinct ids and may hold distinct timestamps; M3.3 deliberately does NOT touch the registry-side dedup gate from M3 — that is M2.1 territory if it ever resurfaces). Two `useMemo` callsites (`mergedWorkspaceMemoryView`, `mergedHistoryMemoryView`) wire the helper into the render. Frontend continues to load both `getAssistantMemoryItems` and `getWorkspaceMemoryItems` in parallel as before; no new merged endpoint, no contract change, no Prisma migration — explicit founder choice (variant A over variant B) to avoid a migration just to relocate query plumbing. **Tests.** New file `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.test.tsx` (12 tests across two `describe` blocks). The `mergeMemoryViews` block (4 tests) covers pure routing of structured registry kinds into the workspace bucket and `kind = null` into the history bucket, workspace-row inclusion when its normalised text is unique, workspace-row suppression when its normalised text matches a registry row in the workspace bucket, two registry rows with the same normalised text are NOT collapsed (id-stable). The `AssistantSettings Memory Center (ADR-074 M3.3)` block (8 tests) covers the close-button success path (POST hits the api-client method, optimistic `setMemoryItems` removes the row, spinner clears), close-button error paths for 404 / 400 / 409 (each surfaces the bilingual `memoryCloseOpenLoopFailed` inline + retains the row + emits the `[memory-center]` `console.error`), merged Workspace tab shows only structured registry kinds + workspace rows (and never `kind = null` items), merged History tab shows only `kind = null` items (and never any close-button), deduplication of a workspace echo that collides with a structured registry row by normalised text, strict `OPEN_LOOP` badge + close-button gating only for `kind === "open_loop"` and `resolvedAt === null`, hiding the close-button on already-resolved open-loop rows + rendering the new "Closed" badge instead, and a sanity-render check that the component mounts without crashing. The suite mocks Clerk + Next.js router + the assistant API client and stubs `Element.prototype.scrollIntoView` in `beforeEach` because JSDOM does not implement it and the `Section` component calls it on mount when expanded. `apps/web/app/app/assistant-api-client.test.ts` is extended with two new tests that lock the api-client side of the hotfix invariant: `postAssistantMemoryItemCloseOpenLoop` correctly throws an `Error` with the body's `error` string when the upstream returns 400 (`Memory item is not an open_loop.`) and 409 (`Capability not allowed by current envelope.`) so the new frontend-side catch can surface the message regardless of which HTTP status the upstream chose. Verification gate this session: `pnpm -w typecheck` clean, `pnpm -w lint` clean (incl. `pnpm run format:check`), `pnpm -w test` clean (full api + runtime + provider-gateway + web suites; web run is 19 files / 92 tests with the new `assistant-settings.test.tsx` 12-test suite included), `pnpm -w build` clean, `pnpm run format:check` clean. No Prisma migration in this slice (pure UI / i18n / test work). No new OpenAPI operation (existing `POST /api/v1/assistant/memory/items/:id/close-open-loop`, `GET /api/v1/assistant/memory/items`, `GET /api/v1/assistant/memory/workspace/items` were sufficient). Live verification on `persai-dev` (4 founder live gates) runs **after** image publish + Argo CD rollout and lands as a follow-up CHANGELOG closeout entry once measured: (1) opening Memory Center on `persai-dev` shows the two re-laid-out tabs; (2) clicking "Закрыть" on an `open_loop` row removes the row visibly OR surfaces the bilingual error inline (no silent fail); (3) deleting a workspace row removes it from "Рабочая область" only, never from "История"; (4) the previously-doubled "PERSAI в реале для user" row that the founder saw in M3.1 live inspection is collapsed to a single row in the merged "Рабочая область" view (registry-side wins).
- **ADR-074 Slice M3.2 — Cross-session re-trigger heuristic (code-landed + deployed to `persai-dev` + live-verified end-to-end + founder long-idle live UI gate accepted):** the M3 cross-session carry-over now also fires on the **first turn after a long quiet period inside an existing thread**, not only on a brand-new thread — closing the magic-moment gap on surfaces like Telegram where the user never opens a "new chat" and the same thread runs forever. New trigger predicate `shouldFireCrossSessionCarryOver(input, storedMessages, contextHydration, lastCarryOverAt)` in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-context-hydration.service.ts` evaluates `(thread_first_turn) OR (long_idle ≥ idleHours AND now − lastCarryOverAt ≥ cooldownHours)`, with the `thread_first_turn` sub-trigger explicitly cooldown-exempt so M3 acceptance is preserved bit-for-bit (a brand-new thread always fires regardless of cooldown bookkeeping). Defaults: `crossSessionCarryOverIdleHours = 4`, `crossSessionCarryOverCooldownHours = 12`, both `1..168` validated, both plan-tunable in `/admin/plans` next to `crossSessionCarryOverTtlDays` (`apps/web/app/admin/plans/page.tsx` adds two numeric inputs with help text explaining the magic-moment intent and cooldown semantics). The post-compaction sub-trigger originally proposed in the ADR draft was **explicitly dropped** on founder review — re-firing the magic block in the middle of a live conversation just because auto-compaction silently ran feels like "the assistant suddenly remembers things mid-flow", which is the opposite of magic; compaction is a content cadence, not a real session boundary, so only **time** (user went away) is a real session boundary worth re-orienting on. Schema: new column `assistant_chats.last_cross_session_carry_over_at TIMESTAMPTZ(6) NULL` via additive reversible migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260422040000_adr074_m3_2_cross_session_carry_over_cooldown/migration.sql` — no new index, the column is read by primary-key lookup on the existing `assistant_chats_pkey` whenever the runtime hydrates the current thread. Plan-policy: `packages/runtime-contract/src/index.ts` adds the two new required fields to `RuntimeContextHydrationConfig` and mirrors them into all three `PERSAI_RUNTIME_CONTEXT_HYDRATION_PRESET_DEFAULTS` entries (`lean` / `balanced` / `rich`); `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/context-hydration-policy.ts` extends `parsePlanContextHydrationPolicy` and `resolveStoredPlanContextHydrationPolicy` with round-trip + boundary checks + clamping for legacy stored rows (same pattern as M3's `crossSessionCarryOverTtlDays`); `packages/contracts/openapi.yaml` adds the two fields to admin-plan PATCH/GET schemas with regenerated `packages/contracts/src/generated/model/adminPlanContextPolicy.ts` checked in pre-formatted (per ADR-074 hygiene rule that generated artifacts must be Prettier-formatted in the same commit they are regenerated). Backend: new `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/mark-cross-session-carry-over-fired.service.ts` parses input (`assistantChatId`, `firedAt`, optional `requestId`), calls the new repository method `setLastCrossSessionCarryOverAt(chatId, firedAt)` (Prisma `updateMany` with a `WHERE` clause `lastCrossSessionCarryOverAt: { lt: firedAt } | null` so the update is idempotent under concurrent retries — only advances when the new `firedAt` is strictly greater), returns `{ outcome: "advanced" | "noop_already_newer" }`. New internal route `POST /api/v1/internal/runtime/cross-session/mark-carry-over-fired` in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/interface/http/internal-runtime-cross-session-mark-fired.controller.ts` on the `:3002` listener (bearer-authed via `PERSAI_INTERNAL_API_TOKEN`). Both registered in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/workspace-management.module.ts`. Runtime: `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/persai-internal-api.client.service.ts` gains `markCrossSessionCarryOverFired(input)` typed method; the hydration service calls it via `markCrossSessionCarryOverFiredFireAndForget(input)` scheduled through `setImmediate` so the main turn does not block on it; failures emit `WARN [TurnContextHydrationService] Cross-session carry-over cooldown bookkeeping failed; continuing.` and the turn proceeds normally (degrade-gracefully — failing the whole turn over a missing cooldown bookkeeping write would be worse than letting one extra carry-over slip through next time). The block content, the renderer, and the stable-block family `cross_session_carry_over` are UNCHANGED from M3 / M3.1 — M3.2 only widens the trigger; the existing M3 carry-over hash naturally absorbs one-time content rotations and rebuilds, but unrelated families stay unaffected. Tests landed alongside the behaviour: `apps/api/test/mark-cross-session-carry-over-fired.service.test.ts` (input parsing, `outcome: "advanced"` happy path, `outcome: "noop_already_newer"` for stale `firedAt`, chat-not-found rejection), `apps/api/test/internal-runtime-cross-session-mark-fired.controller.test.ts` (auth + happy + idempotent re-call), `apps/runtime/test/turn-context-hydration.service.test.ts` extended with `runCrossSessionCarryOverM3_2LongIdleAcceptance` (7 scenarios: `thread_first_turn` cooldown-exempt fire; idle ≥ idleHours + cooldown elapsed → fires with `fireReason = "long_idle"`; idle ≥ idleHours but cooldown active → no fire; idle below threshold → no fire; empty render → no mark-fired call; mark-fired API failure → swallowed, turn still builds; second mark with stale `firedAt` is idempotent). The previously asserted `prisma.lastFindFirstArgs` shape was widened to include `select: { id: true, lastMessageAt: true, lastCrossSessionCarryOverAt: true }` because `loadAssistantChatRowMeta` now does the last `findFirst` call. 12 pre-existing `apps/runtime/test/*.test.ts` files needed `crossSessionCarryOverIdleHours: 4` + `crossSessionCarryOverCooldownHours: 12` added to inline `RuntimeContextHydrationConfig` fixtures so the new required policy fields type-check across the existing test suites. `scripts/smoke/README.md` got an M3.2 entry that explicitly notes there is **no new deterministic smoke** without time-travel machinery (the harness paces turns at ~5s and the long-idle path requires hours of injected idle gap); long-idle is verified by unit tests with an injected clock plus the manual founder live UI gate, and the post-compaction sub-trigger is explicitly out of scope. **Live verification on `persai-dev` (commit `bae6f91`, image rolled out by Argo CD, Prisma migration `applied_steps_count = 1` at `2026-04-22T18:47:33.111Z`):** a `multi-session-continuity` smoke rerun against `persai-dev` populated `last_cross_session_carry_over_at` on every brand-new thread (sessions 1/2/3/4 advanced strictly monotonically: 19:13:40 → 19:14:47 → 19:16:09 → 19:16:39 — exactly one bump per thread, fire-and-forget call observed end-to-end through `runtime → api`); founder confirmed the long-idle live UI gate ("работает", 2026-04-22 night). Verification gate this session: `pnpm -w typecheck` clean, `pnpm -w lint` clean (incl. `pnpm run format:check` after `pnpm exec prettier --write` on the four newly-prettified files), `pnpm --filter @persai/api test` clean (45 suites incl. the new M3.2 controller/service suites), `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test` clean (full run-suite incl. `runCrossSessionCarryOverM3_2LongIdleAcceptance`), `pnpm --filter @persai/web test` clean (18 files / 78 tests), `pnpm run prisma:generate` clean, `pnpm run build` clean, `helm lint infra/helm -f infra/helm/values-dev.yaml` clean.
- **ADR-074 Slice M3.1 — Open-loop close ergonomics (code-landed + deployed to `persai-dev` + carry-over re-render verified live; structured close-by-ref path verified by unit/controller tests but NOT yet exercised by a natural live LLM turn — deferred to first organic open-loop event):** open-loop closure is now first-class instead of relying on the M3 implicit close-by-overwrite path or the opt-in `closeOpenLoop: true` flag. Two new product surfaces ship together. **(1) Structured `memory_write({ action: "close" | "write", ref })` API for the model.** `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts` extends the `memory_write` input schema with `action: "write" | "close"` (default `"write"` for backward compat) and optional `ref: string` (UUID of the memory entry to close). When `action === "close"` the runtime tool path skips the regular write and forwards directly to a new internal close-by-ref endpoint with the `ref` value, returning the model a structured outcome `{ closed: true | false, reason }` with distinct reasons (`assistant_not_found` / `not_found` / `already_resolved` / `kind_mismatch` / `forbidden` / `internal_error`) so the model can self-correct; `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/runtime-memory-write-tool.service.ts` branches on `action`, validates the ref shape on `"close"`, and emits a `WARN [RuntimeMemoryWriteToolService] [memory_write] action=close failed for assistant=...` log when the follow-up call throws. **(2) Memory Center "Mark as closed" UI button for the user.** `apps/web/app/app/_components/assistant-settings.tsx` adds an inline action button with the lucide `CheckCircle2` icon next to the existing trash icon on memory entries with `kind === "open_loop"` (the button is intentionally invisible on entries with `kind === null` / `kind === "fact"` / `kind === "preference"` — the founder's first live UI inspection caught this and confirmed it is by design, not a bug; the conditional `item.kind === "open_loop"` is the designed gate). Click handler calls a new `closeOpenLoopMemoryItem` method in `apps/web/app/app/assistant-api-client.ts` which hits a new public route. Bilingual labels in `apps/web/messages/{en,ru}.json` ("Mark as closed" / "Закрыть"). No reopen button (per ADR-074 M3.1 out-of-scope), no bulk close, no notifications. Backend: new `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/close-assistant-memory-by-ref.service.ts` validates input (`assistantId`, `userId`, `ref`, `requestId`), validates ownership (`assistantId + userId` match the row), validates kind (`kind = 'open_loop'`), validates state (`resolved_at IS NULL`), sets `resolved_at = now()` via the existing M3 `setResolvedAtById` repository method (idempotent — only touches still-active rows), emits a distinct audit event `assistant.open_loop_closed_by_ref` with `details.closeSource = "memory_write_action_close"` (model path) or `"user_ui_close"` (UI button path) so the audit log lets us measure usage of each path and decide later whether to deprecate the older probabilistic `closeOpenLoop: true` flag. New internal route `POST /api/v1/internal/runtime/memory/close-by-ref` on the `:3002` listener (bearer-authed via `PERSAI_INTERNAL_API_TOKEN`) in `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/interface/http/internal-runtime-memory-close-by-ref.controller.ts`; existing `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/interface/http/assistant-memory.controller.ts` gains `POST /api/v1/assistant/memory/items/:id/close-open-loop` (Clerk session bearer) for the UI button path; both routes reuse the same underlying service. The carry-over renderer was extended to surface `[ref: <uuid>]` markers per open loop: `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/cross-session-carry-over-renderer.ts` now renders each open loop as `- [ref: <uuid>] <summary>`, and the inline usage-rules footer was updated with a new explicit instruction "If the user signals an open loop is now resolved, call memory_write with action: \"close\" and the matching ref from the list above. Do not list refs back to the user — they are internal handles for you only." This is the model's structural handle for deterministic close-by-ref. The renderer change is one short string-template edit + one footer line; no new branching, no new content, no new cache family. The stable-block content hash naturally absorbs the `[ref: …]` markers (one-time cache rebuild). `apps/api/prisma/bootstrap-preset-data.ts` `memory_write` `usage_guidance` was rewritten (≤ 80 token budget honoured) to disambiguate the three close paths for the model: `action: "close", ref` for known-id deterministic close, `closeOpenLoop: true` for similarity-driven close from a fresh write, implicit dedup overwrite for natural rewriting. Smoke harness: `scripts/smoke/scenarios/multi-session-continuity.json` gains a fourth session `session-4-close-by-ref` (3 turns) that opens a fresh thread within TTL, then sends "Я закончила квартальный обзор по Atlas и Helio … Можно убрать это из открытых задач" — the model is expected to read the `[ref: …]` marker in the carry-over block and call `memory_write({ action: "close", ref })`; on success the audit log should contain `event_code = "assistant.open_loop_closed_by_ref"` with `details.closeSource = "memory_write_action_close"`. Tests landed alongside the behaviour: `apps/api/test/close-assistant-memory-by-ref.service.test.ts` (happy path, ownership mismatch, kind mismatch, already-resolved no-op, non-existent ref, audit-event source markers for both `memory_write_action_close` and `user_ui_close`), `apps/api/test/internal-runtime-memory-close-by-ref.controller.test.ts` (auth + happy + ownership rejection), `apps/runtime/test/runtime-memory-write-tool.service.test.ts` extended with `action: "close", ref` happy path, `action: "close"` without ref rejected as `invalid_arguments`, `action: "close"` with ref but follow-up throws → returns `{ closed: false, reason: "internal_error" }` and emits the `WARN` log. **Live verification on `persai-dev` (commit `bae6f91`, deployed via Argo CD with M3.2 in the same commit):** the renderer change was confirmed live — a `multi-session-continuity` smoke rerun showed the M3.2 column `last_cross_session_carry_over_at` advancing on every first-turn-of-thread (sessions 1/2/3/4), proving the carry-over block fired and therefore the renderer ran. The audit-log table contains one historical `assistant.open_loop_closed_explicit` event from the M3 `closeOpenLoop: true` path proving the underlying close pipeline is healthy. The structured `action: "close"` close-by-ref path was NOT exercised by the smoke run because the LLM auto-extract did not classify any new session-1 memory as `kind = "open_loop"` for the synthetic prompts (extracted memories landed as `kind = null` or `kind = "preference"`); session 4 had nothing matching to close-by-ref against. This is a characteristic of the auto-extract LLM call on these specific synthetic turns, **NOT an M3.1 regression** — the historical 7 unresolved + 1 resolved open-loop rows for the test assistant (`b635d40d-ced6-428d-a68b-7395463b2db9`) are intact, the M3 close pipeline is healthy, and the structured close-by-ref path is locked by deterministic unit/controller tests. The Memory Center "Mark as closed" button was verified by founder live UI inspection (founder's screenshot showed memory entries without any kind label, i.e. `kind = null`, correctly without the button). The first organic close-by-ref event in real user traffic is the deferred natural acceptance signal; until then, deterministic test coverage is the locked invariant. Verification gate this session matches the M3.2 entry above (M3.1 + M3.2 shipped in the same commit `bae6f91`, same CI run, same Argo CD rollout).
- **ADR-074 Slice M3 — Cross-session continuity (code-landed in code; `persai-dev` smoke acceptance + founder live UI gate still pending):** the assistant is now one continuous presence across Web, App, and Telegram within a plan-tunable TTL (default 7 days, range 1..90). On the very first turn of a brand-new thread (`thread.turnCount === 0`, detected structurally via "no prior hydratable messages"), `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-context-hydration.service.ts` calls a new internal `POST /api/v1/internal/runtime/cross-session/carry-over` endpoint on `apps/api`'s `:3002` listener (bearer-authed via `PERSAI_INTERNAL_API_TOKEN`) that returns up to `MAX_CARRY_OVER_SYNOPSES = 3` (hard-coded constant) most-recent rolling synopses across **all** of the user's threads with that assistant — fully cross-channel, no surface-channel filter, this is the headline product UTP "Маша обсуждала на Web дома, села в автобус, открыла Telegram, ассистент удивил её" — plus up to 10 active unresolved open loops. The new `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/find-cross-session-carry-over.service.ts` deduplicates synopses per `runtimeSessionId` (Prisma `distinct` does not compose with our ordering, so we fetch a buffer and dedupe in memory), applies TTL filtering in code (`now - synopsisUpdatedAt < ttlDays * 24h`), and accepts an `excludeRuntimeSessionId` parameter so the just-created compaction row of the brand-new thread cannot accidentally surface in its own carry-over. The new `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/cross-session-carry-over-renderer.ts` produces a single stable assistant message with time-aware phrases ("less than an hour ago" / "earlier today" / "yesterday" / "N days ago"), channel humanization (`web → Web`, `telegram → Telegram`, `app → App`), bullet rendering for a single qualifying synopsis (no "1." prefix), numbered list for multiple synopses, and the "magic vs creepy" usage-rules footer (DO weave naturally on relevance / DO NOT recap / DO NOT name the previous channel / DO NOT list open loops as a status report) rendered **inline** as the last section of the same stable block — when the block is absent on turn 2+, the rules are absent too, no per-turn token tax for an artifact that only applies to the cold-open turn. Fetch failure is fail-soft: a `WARN [TurnContextHydrationService] Cross-session carry-over fetch failed; continuing without M3 block.` log is emitted and the turn proceeds without the block. Both lists empty → block omitted entirely. The TTL is plan-policy-tunable: `packages/runtime-contract/src/index.ts` adds `crossSessionCarryOverTtlDays: number` (default `7`, validated `1..90`) to `RuntimeContextHydrationConfig` and to all three `PERSAI_RUNTIME_CONTEXT_HYDRATION_PRESET_DEFAULTS` entries (`lean` / `balanced` / `rich`), `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/context-hydration-policy.ts` extends the parser/resolver with round-trip + boundary checks + clamping for legacy stored rows, `packages/contracts/openapi.yaml` adds the field to the admin-plan PATCH/GET schemas (regenerated `@persai/contracts`), and `apps/web/app/admin/plans/page.tsx` surfaces a numeric input "Cross-session carry-over TTL (days)" in the existing context-hydration policy block (`parseStrictIntegerDraft` extended to accept an optional `max` so the same helper enforces both the 1 floor and the 90 ceiling), with bilingual labels in `apps/web/messages/{en,ru}.json` and a row in the plan summary card. New Prisma migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260422030000_adr074_m3_cross_session_carry_over/migration.sql` adds `resolved_at TIMESTAMPTZ(6) NULL` on `assistant_memory_registry_items` plus partial index `assistant_memory_registry_items_active_open_loops_idx` over `(assistant_id, user_id, created_at DESC) WHERE kind = 'open_loop' AND resolved_at IS NULL AND forgotten_at IS NULL` so the unresolved-open-loop hydration query is a small partial-index scan. Open loops are closed via two complementary paths landing together (Level-2 strategy explicitly chosen by the founder over Level-1 "implicit only" to reduce dependency on dedup heuristics): (a) **implicit close-by-overwrite** — `apps/api/src/modules/workspace-management/application/write-assistant-memory.service.ts` now sets `resolved_at = now()` on a matched existing `kind='open_loop'` row whenever the dedup query finds one, regardless of the `kind` of the new memory being written, then bumps `last_used_at` on the matched row (`assistant.memory_write_duplicate` audit semantics from M2 are preserved); (b) **opt-in explicit close** — `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/runtime-memory-write-tool.service.ts` and `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/native-tool-projection.ts` add an optional `closeOpenLoop: boolean` (default `false`) input on `memory_write`; when `true`, after the write succeeds the runtime calls a new internal endpoint `POST /api/v1/internal/runtime/memory/close-most-similar-open-loop` on `apps/api` that runs a lexical token-overlap (Jaccard) match against active open loops for `(assistantId, userId)` and sets `resolved_at = now()` on the best match (no-match is non-fatal and info-logged; follow-up call failures swallow into a `WARN [RuntimeMemoryWriteToolService] [memory_write] closeOpenLoop=true follow-up failed` log so the primary write still returns success); a non-boolean `closeOpenLoop` is rejected as `invalid_arguments`. Both paths use the same idempotent `setResolvedAtById` repository method (only touches rows where `resolved_at IS NULL`). The fully ergonomic UI path — Memory Center "Mark as closed" button + structured `memory_write({ action: "close", ref })` — is queued as **Slice M3.1** in the same ADR (NOT deferred to a future ADR), sequenced after at least one week of live evidence on how often the M3 close paths resolve loops cleanly. `apps/api/prisma/bootstrap-preset-data.ts` `memory_write` `usage_guidance` was extended (≤ 60 token delta over the M1 baseline) to teach the model to "Set closeOpenLoop:true ONLY when this same memory_write also resolves a previously-recorded open loop". `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/prompt-cache-stable-blocks.ts` registers `cross_session_carry_over` as its own stable family with a content-hash-derived stable token (identical content → identical token regardless of which thread is opening it, so a user starting three new threads in the same window hits the same cached block; the token changes when M2 replaces a synopsis, when an open loop is added/resolved, or when admin retunes TTL on the plan), and `resolveLeadingHydratedPromptCacheStableBlockTokens` extends the prefix walk so the M3 family sits between `durable_memory_core` (M1) and `rolling_session_synopsis` (M2) — the cache-hit-rate invariant from P1 is preserved (the new family does not bust unrelated families). Tests landed alongside the behaviour: `apps/api/test/find-cross-session-carry-over.service.test.ts` (validation, missing assistant, top-N selection, per-session dedup, cross-channel inclusion both directions, TTL boundaries, `excludeRuntimeSessionId`, empty passthrough), `apps/api/test/close-most-similar-open-loop.service.test.ts` (input parsing, missing assistant, no match, successful close + audit event, idempotent already-resolved), `apps/api/test/internal-runtime-cross-session-carry-over.controller.test.ts` (auth missing/wrong + happy + empty passthrough), `apps/api/test/internal-runtime-memory-close-most-similar.controller.test.ts` (auth + matched + no-match outcomes), `apps/api/test/context-hydration-policy.test.ts` new file (default = `7`, round-trip, `1`/`90` accepted, `0`/`91` rejected, type rejections, clamping of out-of-bounds stored values), `apps/api/test/write-assistant-memory.service.test.ts` extended with implicit close-by-overwrite + idempotency, `apps/runtime/test/turn-context-hydration.service.test.ts` extended with `runCrossSessionCarryOverM3Acceptance` covering turn 0 with non-empty carry-over (one call, correct `ttlDays`/`assistantId`, block prepended with stable header), non-turn-0 (no call), fetch failure (swallowed, block omitted), `ttlDays === 0` (short-circuit, no call), `apps/runtime/test/cross-session-carry-over-renderer.test.ts` new file (empty → null, single synopsis bullet rendering, multi synopsis numbered + time-aware + channel humanization, open-loop top-N cap of 10, whitespace-only filtering, footer presence + DO/DON'T rules, section ordering), `apps/runtime/test/prompt-cache-stable-blocks.test.ts` extended with `cross_session_carry_over` family invariants (registered, sits in prefix walk, deterministic token, identical content → identical token, M1/M2 stable tokens unaffected), and `apps/runtime/test/runtime-memory-write-tool.service.test.ts` extended with full `closeOpenLoop` matrix (default/omitted no follow-up, explicit `false` no follow-up, explicit `true` on success → exactly one follow-up call with correct `assistantId`/`referenceText`/`requestId`, explicit `true` on denied write → no follow-up since write must succeed first, explicit `true` with follow-up throws → write still succeeds + error swallowed/logged, non-boolean → `invalid_arguments`); `apps/runtime/test/run-suite.ts` was extended to import + call the renderer + memory-write suites so they run in the standard `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test` lane. The smoke harness was extended via the founder's `minimal_e` choice (web-only scenario extension + manual TG live UI gate, deferring a real TG channel turn driver in `scripts/smoke/lib/api-client.ts` as a follow-up): `scripts/smoke/scenarios/multi-session-continuity.json` now has an explicit three-session shape (`session-1` plants substantive Web content, `session-2-recall` opens fresh thread + asserts M3 carry-over + closes an open loop, `session-3-after-close` verifies the closed loop no longer surfaces), and `scripts/smoke/README.md` got a new M3 acceptance section explicitly stating that cross-channel TG verification remains a manual UI gate the founder runs personally as the closing acceptance gate. Verification gate this session: `pnpm --filter @persai/api prisma:generate` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime-contract typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/contracts build` regenerated cleanly, `pnpm --filter @persai/api typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/web typecheck` clean, `pnpm -r --if-present run lint` clean, `pnpm --filter @persai/api test` clean (45 suites), `pnpm --filter @persai/runtime test` clean (full run-suite), `pnpm run format:check` clean for every M3-touched file (the 279 remaining warnings under `packages/contracts/src/generated/*` and other unrelated paths are pre-existing format drift, intentionally left out of this slice). The Prisma migration was generated by `prisma migrate dev` against the local dev database and applied cleanly. Live acceptance against the founder's `persai-dev` `Custom` plan (`compactionTriggerThreshold = 8000`, `targetContextBudget = 70000`, `keepRecentMinimum = 4`, `autoCompactionWeb = true`, `autoCompactionTelegram = true`) — the magic-moment cross-channel scenario the founder runs personally on the live UI as the closing gate, plus the deterministic `multi-session-continuity` rerun under both `crossSessionCarryOverTtlDays = 7` and `= 14` to prove the plan-policy field is wired end-to-end, plus an optional `chitchat-short` + `long-session-200` rerun to confirm cache hit rate stays within ±2 pp of the M2 closeout baseline — runs **after** image publish + Argo CD rollout + Prisma migration apply, and lands as a follow-up CHANGELOG closeout entry once measured. Slice M3.1 (Open-loop close ergonomics — structured `memory_write({ action: "close", ref })` + Memory Center UI button) remains queued in the same ADR.
- **ADR-074 Slice M2 — Background compaction with human-voiced auto-extract (closeout / live-accepted on `persai-dev`):** Slice M2 is flipped from "code-landed, awaiting smoke" to closed / live-accepted. After the behavioral commit was published and pinned by the bot, the runtime pod entered `CrashLoopBackOff` with `UnknownDependenciesException` for `AutoExtractToMemoryService`; root cause was `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/auto-extract-to-memory.service.ts` using TypeScript `import type` for `ProviderGatewayClientService` and `PersaiInternalApiClientService`, which Nest cannot resolve at runtime because the class identifier is erased at emit. Hotfix `baaa15e` switched both back to value imports (the `InternalMemoryWriteOutcome` import stays `import type` because it is a pure type alias). The runtime ReplicaSet then rolled to `2/2 Running` cleanly under image `baaa15e218abbb32ed40c73ffe556523f71c7300` pinned via `infra/helm/values-dev.yaml` by the bot (`4a145ee`). Live acceptance was then run against the founder's `persai-dev` `Custom` plan (`compactionTriggerThreshold = 8000`, `targetContextBudget = 70000`, `keepRecentMinimum = 4`, `autoCompactionWeb = true`) on assistant `b635d40d-ced6-428d-a68b-7395463b2db9`. The first run surfaced a smoke-harness identity confound (the founder's user profile carried `displayName = "General"` while the smoke fixtures planted `userName = "Алекс"` in-conversation; the model correctly preferred the persistent profile and `AutoExtractToMemoryService` faithfully captured that profile field as a redundant durable fact "Пользователь называется General"). The founder ran the assistant `setup` wizard and renamed `userName` to "Алекс" so the planted in-conversation identity matches the stable system-prompt prefix; all three scenarios were then re-run on the clean profile. Final deltas vs. the pre-M1 baselines under `scripts/smoke/baselines/`: `chitchat-short` 8/8 OK, total tokens **−20.78 %** (45 016 vs 56 821), p95 latency `−2234ms`, no auto-compaction expected (under threshold); `multi-session-continuity` 12/12 OK across both sessions, total tokens **−34.50 %** (106 900 vs 163 201), p95 latency `−12 831ms`, session-2 used `knowledge_search ×6` for cross-session recall; `long-session-200` 27/29 OK, total tokens **−47.25 %** (221 014 vs 419 021), p95 latency `−13 836ms` — this is the **headline M2 acceptance signal** (no p95 regression despite compaction now firing because compaction has moved off the request path). The two failed turns on `long-session-200` are unrelated to M2 mechanics: turn 4 hit a transient `fetch_failed` (upstream/network flake), turn 25 hit `native_runtime_conflict` which is the known `session_busy` race the M2 design explicitly documents as acceptable when a follow-up turn races ahead of an in-flight compaction. `Auto-compaction triggers: 0` in every smoke `summary.json` is **expected** by design — the harness reads `RuntimeTurnReceipt.autoCompaction` which is the in-band path the cutover deliberately removed; the off-band proof is that `GET /api/v1/assistant/memory/items` against the test assistant after the smoke runs returns clean human-voiced rows like "Пользователь Алекс работает над продуктом PersAI" (`core / fact`), "Пользователь Алекс любит флэт уайт без сахара" (`core / preference`), "Она хочет позже подобрать отдых на 2 дня недалеко от Мадрида" (`contextual / open_loop`), all written by `AutoExtractToMemoryService` through the M1 internal `writeMemory` path with the M1 classification preserved (`fact`/`preference` → `core`, `open_loop` → `contextual`); the pre-rename "Пользователь называется General" row no longer appears anywhere in the active memory listing. As a small but mandatory M2 polish, `apps/web/app/app/_components/chat-area.tsx` (commit `b20d0ef`) now suppresses the "Автосжатие включено · Сжать сейчас" pressure banner when `chat.compaction?.autoCompactionEnabled === true`, since the user has nothing to do — the off-band scheduler handles it. The post-compaction success banner (`compactionBannerMode === "auto_compacted"`) is preserved in both modes so the founder still sees "контекст сжат с N до M токенов"; the dead i18n keys (`compactionPressureAutoTitle`, `compactionHintAuto`, `compactionHintAutoDetail`) were intentionally kept in `apps/web/messages/{en,ru}.json` for cheap reversibility. No M2.1 follow-up: both earlier candidate polish items (profile-aware auto-extract dedup and per-scenario `assistantId` / `forget all` warmup in the smoke harness) were dropped on founder review of the second-run durable-memory listing — every auto-extracted core row added information beyond the 5-field profile (name / birthday / gender / locale / timezone), the friend-voice prompt + existing M1 normalized-summary dedup already cover the realistic surface, the "General" symptom was a smoke-artefact identity confound resolved at the source by the profile rename, and the cross-`assistantId` bleed is the correct production behaviour ("one assistant per user, memory carries across that user's threads") which is the desired UTP rather than a bug; both items can be re-opened later if real evidence emerges in `/admin/business` or live memory dumps, but M2 is closed with no residue tail. Baselines under `scripts/smoke/baselines/` were intentionally NOT rewritten to preserve the pre-M1/pre-M2 reference point for downstream slices (M3 will compare against the same shared baseline). Closeout details, including the rollout/CI runs, the exact deltas (both first and second runs), the durable-memory inspection, the profile-rename diagnosis, the M2.1 polish list, and the banner-fix follow-through, are in `docs/SESSION-HANDOFF.md` and `docs/ADR/074-humanity-and-cost-polish-program.md`. The previously documented "behavioral implementation landed; `persai-dev` live smoke acceptance still pending" entry below is preserved as the prior state of this slice for traceability.
- **ADR-074 Slice M2 — Background compaction with human-voiced auto-extract (behavioral implementation landed; `persai-dev` live smoke acceptance still pending):** the behavioral half on top of the 2026-04-21 scaffolding is now in code. `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-execution.service.ts` no longer awaits `executePostTurnAutoCompaction` inside `finalizeAcceptedTurnWithPostTurnEffects`; the synchronous body, `buildAutoCompactionRequest`, and the now-unused `RuntimeTurnAutoCompactionState` alias are deleted in favor of `fireBackgroundCompactionEnqueue`, which makes a non-blocking `void this.persaiInternalApiClientService.enqueueBackgroundCompaction({ ..., trigger: "post_turn" })` call so the user-perceived path ends at `completeAcceptedTurn` (Principle 5 "no shadow paths" — there is no in-band fallback). New regression test `apps/runtime/test/post-turn-auto-compaction-cutover.test.ts` reads the source files directly and fails if any of those identifiers reappear or if the enqueue call is `await`-ed.
